After I have completed this book for you, my Sons, which is the last in the science of medicine with its complement, and I have reached the end of it according to its exposition and declaration, it seemed to me that I should complete it with this Tractate, which is a part of the operation, namely surgery with the hand.
Because the operation by hand has fallen into disuse in our region and time, so that perhaps its knowledge has perished and its trace has been cut off; and nothing of it remains except small descriptions in the books of the ancients, which hands have changed, and error and hesitation have befallen them until their intentions were closed and their power was distant. It seemed to me that I should revive this science with the arrangement of this Tractate in it according to the way of exposition, declaration, and abbreviation; and that I come with the forms of the tools of cautery and the other instruments of work: as is done by the addition of declarations and their hastening.
The reason why a good artisan of it is not found with his hand in this our time is that the art of medicine is long, and its author must be trained beforehand in the science of anatomy, as Galen has narrated, until he knows the supports of the limbs and their forms, and their conjunction and separation, and has knowledge of the bones, and nerves, and sinews, and their number, and their exit, and the pulsatile and quiet veins, and the places of their exit.
And because of that, Hippocrates said: "The name with the name is much, and with work it is little, especially in the art of hand.
But we have already spoken about this at the beginning of this book.
"For one who is not skilled in anatomy may fall into error, by which people are killed: as I have seen many of those who boast about this skill without knowledge or experience.
"That is, because I saw a foolish physician cut out a scrofulous abscess on a woman's neck and he cut some of the arteries in the neck; therefore the blood flowed from the woman until she died in his hands.
"And I saw another physician who dared to remove a stone from a man who had grown old, and the stone was large. "So he came to him and removed it with a piece of the bladder. "Therefore the man died on the third day.
"And indeed I had already been called to remove it; and seeing the size of the stone and the condition of the patient, I knew that he would die.
"And I saw another physician who was receiving a fee from a certain Duke of our land for his medical skill; and it happened that the Duke's black eunuch had a fracture in his leg near the heel: and the physician hastened with his ignorance, and bound up the fracture on the wound with bandages and tight cords, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
"Then he released him according to his wishes. "After a few days he dismissed him and instructed him not to loosen the bandage; and it remained so until his leg became swollen, as well as his foot, and it came to ruin.
"So I was called to him; and I hastened to loosen the bandage; and he was restored to peace, and escaped from his pains.
"However, the corruption had already set in the limb; and I could not prevent it.
Thus, when the corruption ceased wandering through the limb, until it died.
And I saw another physician, who punctured a cancerous abscess: and after some days it ulcerated, until its evil grew great with its lord.
That is, because when it is a pure cancer of black bile, then one must not approach it with iron at all, unless it is in a member that can endure it, so that the whole of it may be cut out.
And for this reason, O Sons, it is necessary for you to know that the operation with the hand is divided into two divisions: namely, the operation which is associated with health, and the operation with which there is danger in many cases.
And I have already pointed out in every place of this book where the operation comes which has terror and fear.
Therefore it is necessary for you to beware of that and abandon it, so that the foolish may not find a way to speak and dishonor it.
Receive therefore the measure with diligence and care, and your weak ones with ease and strength, and use the better way leading by God's grace to health and praiseworthy success: and put away terrible diseases that are difficult to cure: and lift up your spirits from that which makes you afraid, so that hesitation may not enter upon you in your faith and advantage. xspace
For it is more lasting to your glory, and higher in this world, and finally to your quantities.
For Galen has already said this in some of his warnings. Do not treat the disease badly, lest you be called bad physicians.
Now, however, I have divided this Treatise into three Chapters.
Chapter One
Of the Cautery with fire, and of the Cautery with sharp medicine, arranged and ordered from the head to the feet, and with forms of instruments and tools of the Cautery: and everything necessary for the operation.
Chapter Two.
On incisions and punctures, bloodletting and cupping, wounds, and the extraction of arrows and similar things; all arranged according to the shapes of the instruments.
Chapter Three.
On the restoration of dislocations and the treatment of twists, and similar things; arranged by parts from head to foot and according to the shapes of the instruments.
But before remembering the use of cautery, it is necessary to say what its beneficial and harmful qualities are, and in which constitution it should be used.
I say therefore that the discourse on the quality of the benefit and harm of cautery is a lengthy, subtle, scientific, and hidden secret.
Many wise men have spoken about it and differed on the subject, and for me a little of their speech is enough, fearing lengthiness. ︎
I say therefore that cautery is beneficial to every constitution, whether material or immaterial, except for two constitutions: a hot constitution without matter and a dry constitution without matter.
But in a hot and dry constitution with matter they differed. For some have said that cautery is beneficial in it. And others said the opposite, that is, that cautery is not suitable for an illness caused by heat and dryness; since the nature of fire is heat, and it is inappropriate to heal a hot and dry illness with what is hot and dry.
And the one who speaks against that says: that by cautery there is a benefit in every hot and dry disease which occurs in human bodies; because when you compare the human body and its humors to the nature of fire, you find the human body cold.
And I say through his statement: because experience has revealed this to me many times.
However, it is not necessary that this be attempted except by one who has already been tested and practiced in the last exercise of cautery, and knows the diversity of human complexions, and the nature of diseases within them, and their causes, and their symptoms, and the duration of time for them.
From the other complexions there is no need to fear, especially in cold and moist diseases. For all doctors have agreed upon them; and they have not disagreed about the benefit of cautery in those cases.
And know, my sons, that the secret of treatment by cautery with fire and its goodness is superior to cautery with burning medicine, because fire is simple, whose action does not extend except to the member which is cauterized; and it does not harm another connected member, unless with slight harm.
But the action of burning medicine extends to what is distant from the members; and perhaps it brings about disease in the member which is difficult to heal, and perhaps it kills.
But fire, because of its subtlety and the goodness of its substance, does not do this except in excess.
Indeed, we have learned this through experience because of the length of our service and study with art, and our commitment to the truth of things; and for that reason I am excused from further discourse.  />  />
And if it were not so, because it is not permitted to this book of mine, I would bring you the hidden secret in fire, and the quality of its operation in expelling humors from the body, demonstrated with philosophical discourse which would be understood by your minds.
And know, my sons, that they disagree about the time when it is suitable to perform cautery, and they consider spring to be a better time.
And I say that cautery is suitable at any time; for the harm caused by the time will be overwhelmed by the benefit derived from cautery. And especially if cautery is necessary because of severe and persistent pains that do not tolerate delay; for fear that from them something worse may occur than the slight harm caused by the time.
And let it not enter your minds, my sons, that only the common and foolish physicians think so; namely, that the disease which is cured by cautery does not always return: and they put forward this consequence, but it is not as they think; because cautery is only in the place of medicine, which alters the complexion and dries up the humors which are the causes of pains.
Nevertheless, cautery excels medicine in the swiftness of its effect, and the power of its action, and the strength of its dominion: and it is possible for the disease to return at some time according to the complexion of the patient, and the location of his disease, and its power; and what has been prepared in his body through the accumulation of superfluous humors in him; and what reaches him from his food and similar causes, unless the disease is one in which cautery is applied.
A slight disease of a member with few superfluous humors and moisture, such as tooth cautery for pain, and similar conditions, it is possible that this pain will not return. But this happens rarely.
But the common saying that cautery is the last resort of medicine is true; not in the sense they intend by it; for they believe that there is no cure which is as effective as medicine or any other treatment after cautery has been applied. (){#}
"The truth of the matter is contrary to this, and the intent is that cautery is the last resort in medicine; it is not used unless when we apply methods of healing for some ailments, those remedies do not work. Then at the end, we apply cautery, and it helps. Therefore, it follows that cautery is the last resort in medicine, not according to the intention that the common people and most ignorant physicians understand.
"The ancients said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron; and they did not say this except because of the equality of gold and the nobility of its substance. They also said that the site of the cautery does not become inflamed. "In truth, this is not absolutely the case; for I have already tested it and found that, in some bodies, it does so without any other cause.
"And cautery with gold is good and better than with iron, as they said. "However, when you use a cautery made of gold in the fire, it does not indicate to you when it has reached the desired heat because of the redness of the gold; and if it cools down too quickly, and if you add more fire, it melts in the flame and turns into layers.
"For this reason, the craftsman falls into difficulty with it; and for this reason, cautery made of iron is quicker and more convenient for us, being suitable for the operation.
"And I have already arranged this chapter on the cautery according to chapters, and I have arranged them from head to foot, so that they may provide relief for those seeking something from it.
"Chapter Two
"This cauterization is beneficial for controlling moisture and coldness over the brain, which are two causes of headaches, excessive flow of humors to the eyes and ears, too much sleep, toothache, throat pain, and universally all ailments that occur from coldness, such as paralysis, headaches, epilepsy, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
The method of cauterization is as follows: first instruct the patient to evacuate with a cleansing purgative for three or four nights, according to the strength of the patient, their age, and their habit.
Then instruct him to shave his head with a razor. Then have him sit facing you, with his hands placed on his chest.
Then place the root of your palm over the root of his nose between his eyes. Wherever your middle finger reaches, mark that spot with ink.  />  And do this three times in succession.
Then prepare the cautery iron for the fire: its form is as follows.
Then place it on the marked spot with ink, gradually tightening your hand as you turn it. Then quickly lift your hand and look at the spot.
If you see that the bone has been exposed to the size of a lentil or a grain of barley, then lift your hand. And if not, repeat with the same iron or another one if this one has cooled down: until you see the bones I mentioned to you.
Then take some salt, dissolve it in water, soak a cloth in it, and place it on the spot: and leave it there for three days.
Then place a cloth soaked in butter over it, and leave it on the spot until the scar of the fire is destroyed.  /> Then treat it with four-ingredient ointment until it heals.
They say that the more open the wound remains, the more pus is released, which is better and more beneficial.
And some say that the skin should be cauterized all the way to the bone, and that the cautery should be held until something of the thickness of bone is burned.
Then it is scraped from the burned area of the bone, then it is cleaned.
And others say that one should use the cautery until it reaches the end, so that it makes an impression on the bone in the shape of a circle: or they use a small instrument that women place into infusions of alphabet letters; and they believe that the vapors of the head are expelled from this location, and the wound should be left open for a long time.
Then it should be cleaned until it heals.
But these two types of cautery seem to me not at all except in some people according to the way of fear.
And leaving it is better for me with his health.
The head is weakened by the dissolution of its natural continuity, as we have testified with other members; and especially when the head is naturally weak due to illness. The first type of cautery, however, is safer and better for me, and I use it. Therefore, operate with it in safety.
Chapter 3
When a chronic and persistent pain occurs in the whole head of the patient, and he makes use of hyeres (a type of poultice), coches (ointments or unguents), head purges, oils, and emplastrums (medicated plasters). And especially if it has already been cauterized with the one-pronged cautery that we have described, and none of those things help him, then consider this. For if the patient's head is of a strong natural constitution and not weak, and he finds severe cold, then cauterize him with another cautery under that one, in a small amount. Then cauterize him over every horn of his head with the cautery, so that it does not penetrate through the skin, and expose a quantity from the bone as we have described. And burn it with one cautery on the back of his head, in the place called vas: and lift up your hand in this manner, and do not expose the mouth. For the patient will find on account of this a very severe pain, and different from the pain of all other head cauteries.
And I call this cautery the one for its place: and it should be a cautery that is finer than the one used to cauterize the horns of the head and its back.
Chapter Four
When pain occurs on one side of the head or extends to the eye and is evacuated with purgative drugs, and the remaining treatment as I mentioned in the divisions of diseases is not effective, then cautery for this condition is according to two methods: either cautery with a burning, acute drug; or with iron. 》
The cautery with a burning, acute drug is as follows: take one tooth of garlic and peel it, and cut off the tips from both sides of it. Then split the painful place in time with a wide fleam until there is made under the skin a space in which to insert the tooth.
Insert it under the skin until it is hidden; then tie over it with a suitable bandage; and leave it for fifteen hours; then untie it, and extract the garlic, and let the wound be left open for two days, or three; then place on it cotton soaked in butter until the place produces pus; then treat it with ointment until it is healed. 》
And if you wish to do this with some burning drugs that I have written about in the twelfth treatise, on Burning Medicines.
The cauterization of it with iron is done in this manner. A cautery of fire, the form of which is this.
And it is called a nail-shaped cautery because the form of its head is like that of a nail, in which there is something of curvature, and in the middle of it is a small projection.
Then place it on the spot and hold your hand steady; and you revolve the iron little by little with speed; and let the quantity that is burned be from the thickness of the skin, as its half. And lift your hand so that the artery below is not burned and a flow of blood occurs.
Then soak a piece of cotton in salt water and place it on the spot and leave it for three days; then place the cotton with butter; afterwards treat it with ointment until it heals.
And if you wish, cauterize this half of the skull with the tip of a small knife similar to the cautery. And beware of cutting an artery in this half of the skull, not properly ancient.
§ On the manner of cauterizing in the old half of the skull.
When you treat the half of the skull with what we have said in the previous treatment and what we have said in the divisions of diseases, and the treatment does not help; and you see from the disease that what we have said from the first cautery with medicine or with the cautery with fire is not enough for it, then you must heat a knife-shaped cautery until it turns white after you mark on the spot of pain with a line whose length is half a finger, or almost like that; and lift your hand once, and press it until you cut the artery and reach the bone.
Nevertheless, it is necessary for you to beware of the continuation of the jawbone that moves during chewing, lest the side or the nerve that moves it be burned and a spasm occur.
"And let it be over a cover, as a precaution against bleeding from the cut artery. "For its incision is fearsome, especially for one who does not know what he is doing and is neither diligent nor experienced; and he abandons the operation first of all.
"And I will discuss the regulation of bleeding from an artery according to its manner and in the appropriate place in this book.
"But if you see from the illness that this cautery is not enough, and you see the patient's body enduring the cautery on the middle of the head, as we have described, take care of the wound until it heals.
"And if you wish, administer the cautery that we mentioned in the chapter on extracting an artery with a double-bladed cautery. "For cauterization is better and more beneficial this way.
"On the method of cauterizing for ear pain.
"When ear pain occurs from cold and is treated with dissolving remedies and the other treatments we mentioned in the division, and the pain does not go away, then apply fire cautery. And this is what is called a 'punch,' which has this shape.
"Then apply the punch after its burning around the entire ear, as it is shown; or around both ears if the pain is simultaneous in both. "And keep the cautery away from the root of the ear for a short while after marking the spots with wax; and let the number of punctures be ten on each ear, as shown.
"Then care for the spots until they heal.
"On the method of cauterizing for toothache.
Chapter VII.
"The toothache that is treated with cauterization is only from the types that occur from phlegm, as we said in the divisions of diseases.
And avoid cauterization for conditions caused by dryness and nerve spasm.
When you treat this type of pain with herbs, and head washes, and gargles, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, a second a little lower than its tympanum, and a third at the junction of the two lips.
And place your cautery on the opposite side from the afflicted area. Because softening occurs only in the part that appears healthy.
And the method of cauterization is that you cauterize with a cautery directly on the upper edge of the ear, a little below the horn of the head; and another in the tympanum, whose length should be according to the length of the thumb. And place your hand with the cautery until the thickness of half the skin is burned.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is a species made from a knife, whose form has been described; however, it is not somewhat thinner than that which you see, and it must be a knife with a little excess thickness.
Then treat the places with what has been mentioned until they heal.
¶ On the method of cauterizing for an old stroke.
When the stroke has become old, and you treat it with what we have mentioned, and your treatment does not help, and the patient does not have a fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries on every horn of his head, and a cautery in the middle of the head as we have said, and a cautery in the back of the head, according to what has been described: and the method of cauterization is according to what has been described. 》
And also cauterize with a cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and this is the most important [cautery]. 》
Then it should be scraped with what precedes it.
Chapter 9.
It is necessary that first of all, large doses of horehound and pills cleansing the brain be given to the patient to drink.
Then shave the whole head of the patient and place upon his occiput a plaster made of mustard, as described in the treatise on plasters; and repeat this several times.
For this is the method of cautery, and perform it in the same way as I mentioned there.
If therefore he is cured by this, that is good. If not, then make three cauteries on the back of his head, which should descend from the upper part of the head to the lower part of the eye; and place between each cautery a thickness like that of a finger.
Then treat the cauteries with what preceded.
But if you wish to add to it and the patient can tolerate it, then make a cautery in the middle. If you wish to add (to it), then cauterize him on both temples.
Then treat (the patient) until he is cured; and let the cautery be anointed with oil according to the aforesaid form.
¶ On the method of cauterizing for paralysis and flaccidity.
Chapter 10. ︎
It is necessary that you proceed with the cleansing of the head using horehound and as we have said. ︎
Then shave the head of the patient; afterwards cauterize him with a cautery in the middle of his head and a cautery on each temple, and a cautery on the back of his head, and three cauteries on the nape of the neck.
But if you need (to do) many things in the illness of flaccidity of the body, and the patient can tolerate it, and the illness is strong, then cauterize him with four cauteries on the nape of his back, and the last one until it burns most of his skin, and lift your hand. ︎  Then care for him until he is healed: and thus apply the cautery oil.
On the Method of Cauterizing for Epilepsy
An epileptic is not cauterized unless his epilepsy is due to phlegm.
Therefore, you should first cleanse his brain with hyeros and with the other treatment that we have mentioned in the division, when the patient is large or is able to take medicines.
But if he is a child who does not tolerate medicines, then give him a gargle and cleansing foods to chew for many days before that with the improvement of his food.
Then shave his head, afterward cauterize him with one cautery in the middle of his head, as has been mentioned before in the manner: and with another cautery on his nape, and on each horn of his head with a cautery. If the patient is strong and tolerates it, then cauterize him with the cauteries that I have mentioned for one who has paralysis, and apply softening to his body over the vertebrae of the neck and the vertebrae of the back; and let the cautery oil be according to the manner that has been mentioned.  />
But if the patient is a child, then place a subtle cautery, in this manner.
¶ On the Method of Cauterizing for Melancholy
When the cause of melancholy is foul moisture and thick phlegm, then cauterize him with the cauteries that we have mentioned for one who has paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is an excess flowing down to the melancholy, and his body is moist, then give him in drink what cleanses his brain, as has been mentioned before in the division: then shave the head of the patient, and make afterward a nicely made ring from linen, like a circle.  />
Then place it on top of the head; and let the patient, seated on a stool, be held firmly from every side.
Then present the ointment. And it is better made with ancient goose fat. And heat the ointment over a moderate fire to the degree that a finger can bear when inserted into it. Then evacuate it onto the middle of his head in a circle, and leave it until it cools down.
Do this for the patient once every week, along with the rest of his good diet, until he is healed.
Or if you wish, cauterize it by making many small points on it, except that you should hold the hand with the cautery; indeed, it should be smelling.
For this kind of cautery moistens the brain with its quality.
Then place upon it a compress soaked in butter or chicken fat.
¶ On the method of cauterizing with descending water to the eye.
Chapter 13
When the beginning of water in the eye is declared to you through the signs which I mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient to drink along with something that will cleanse his head.
And keep him away from all moisture and make him sit in a bath while fasting for some days.
Then instruct him to shave his head, and cauterize him on the middle of his head. 》 Then cauterize him over both temples with two cauteries, if the descent of water begins in both eyes at once; or on one side, if it begins in only one eye: and cut off all the veins and arteries which are under the skin with the cautery; and let the cauteries be long in the width of the temples; and beware of bleeding. 》
If you see anything from it, then cut him off immediately with whatever medicine is possible; and I will come with the wisdom that is in extracting the arteries, and cutting them off, and being careful of bleeding.
And sometimes it is cauterized in the neck, under two bones, with two cauteries completely extended.
On the way of cauterizing the old tears.
When the tears of the eyes are old and constant, and they are on the veins and arteries which are externally visible on the forehead, it is verified that this is from cold and phlegmatic excesses; then cauterize with the same cautery as I narrated in the beginning for descending water, one cautery in the middle of the forehead, and two cauteries above the temples, and two cauteries in the neck under the bones. And if you need an addition, then cauterize it on every side of the eye, above the outer edge of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
On the way of cauterizing nose stench.
When you treat it with what we said in the section on division and the treatment is not beneficial, then hurry and give infirmocochias to drink for three nights; afterwards shave his head and cauterize him with a medium cautery, and with an olive oil cautery. Then cauterize him with two nail-shaped cauteries on the outer edges of the eyebrows under a few hairs.
And be careful not to cut into the artery.
And this is the shape of the nail-shaped cautery.
On the way of cauterizing for softening the eyelid. ‌
When the eyelid of the eye is softened from illness or moisture, then cauterize the eyelid with one cautery, and this lunar-shaped cautery. ‌
And if you wish, cauterize it a little on the outer edges of both eyebrows with two cauteries all around; and let them be distant from the temples; and let the length of every cautery be according to the length of the eyebrow; and do not bring your hand to an end with the cautery, rather according to the amount that is burnt on the third eyelid. ‌
About the way of cauterizing the eyelid when the hair turns back and pricks the eye.
The caustic in it is according to two methods: either the caustic with fire, or the caustic with burning medicine.
But in the caustic with fire, first instruct the patient to let their hairs grow out, if they are among those who pluck them, until they lengthen and even out. But if they prick him at their growth, then bind his eyes with a ribbon so that they do not move until they are born.
Therefore, when they are born and even out, then place the patient's head in your lap; then mark on his eyelids with encaustic, a mark like the shape of a myrtle leaf, and let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs.
Then place a cotton soaked in egg white or in the mucilage of fleawort over the eye. ¶ Et sic cauterizabis eum, et sanabitur.
Then the caustic with fire, whose shape is this:
Then cauterize over the shape that you have marked little by little in many times, until the skin surface, which is like the shape of a myrtle leaf, becomes completely evident.
And the sign of health of your work is: if you see the eyelid of the eye already contracting and the hairs lifting from the pricking point of the eye.
Then lift your hand; and leave him for three days. ¶ Deinde adiungas ei, in uino cum zibado, puluerem aloes de quattuor partibus, et mellis de uno: et mitte illum per nares.
Then place a cotton with butter on it, until the scab is removed. Then care for him with ointment, until he is healed.
If any hair grows back after an hour and the eyelid softens, then repeat the cautery on that spot as you did first.
But if the hairs are on the lower (eyelid), then cauterize it until it is raised to its natural place, and it is even so that the hairs do not prick the eye.
It is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow until they are lengthened and evened out. Make from linen cloth the shape of a myrtle leaf.
Then take from known soap and from unmixed lime a weight of one ounce or about that amount from each; then grind them together well until they become like this quickly, so that it does not cool down. Then spread the paste from this onto the linen cloth you made in the shape of a myrtle leaf, and place it on the eyelid of one or two eyes. ︎ And place under the eye a compress soaked in egg white, and let the patient's head rest on your lap.
And place your index finger on the medicine, and press it briefly. And you move it whenever the patient feels the burning of the medicine, for its burning is like fire.
While this persists, which the patient finds to be a burning sensation, then remove the medicine and move it with your finger. When the burning sensation has subsided, then remove the medicine, and wash the eye with water. ︎ ︎
And then consider if you see the eyelid being raised, as it is raised by contracting with fire or with incision; that is good. And if not, then repeat the medicine on the same spot where the medicine does not imprint and does not darken, until your work becomes even and the eye contracts. ︎ ︎ ︎
Then place on it the kohl with butter until the skin of the burn is removed. Then treat it with diaphoretic ointment or another until it heals.
And it is necessary for you during the treatment that you guard with the highest care lest anything from the medicine fall into the eye.
And if the eyelid softens after some days and something from the hairs enters into the eye, then repeat the medicine on that place which becomes softened from the eyelid as you did at first. Then treat it until it heals.
And this is the form of a myrtle leaf.
And know that the eyes of men differ in size and smallness. Therefore let your consideration be according to this, and the way of righteousness shall not be hidden from him who is dedicated to this art.
¶ On the Method of Cauterizing the Tear Duct.
When you treat the fistula with what we have said in the divisions of diseases and your treatment does not succeed: then it is necessary for you to cauterize it according to this method.
Instruct the patient to place his head in your lap, and let an assistant hold his head between his hands so that it does not move or shake with his head.
Then place kohl mixed in the white of an egg or in slippery elm mucilage on his eye; then with a cautery iron, whose form is this. ➤
Let it be hollow like the form of a vulture feather from one end, with which is made the cautery; and if its strength is to penetrate to the other end, and if its strength is upward thus do you try.
However, this hollow (one) is better for your work.
Then express the fistula if it is open, and draw out its pus, and dry it; and if it is not open, then open it, and draw out its pus. ➤
Then place a hot cautery on it.
And hold the cautery with your hand near the eye and towards the nose, so that your hand does not wander or disturb the patient; and place the cautery on the eye fat and burn it.
If you reach the beginning of the vein all the way to the mouth, it will be well. And if not: then repeat the cautery once or twice, if you need it; and leave it for three days.
Then put a compress with butter on it, and care for him with a drying ointment until he is healed.
But if forty days have passed and he is not healed, then place a sharp corrosive medicine on it until the mouth is uncovered; and scrape it according to its chapter.
And there is another method of cautery for a fistula, which some have said first. Find the place of the fistula and locate it; then put a thin camahan, that is, a thin cannula, whose form is this. ➤ And pour into it the quantity of a drachm of molten lead, and hold your hand with the canula firmly, so that the patient is not moved at all, lest the molten lead run or reach his eye. ➤
And it is necessary to put a compress soaked in egg white or water on the patient's eye.
For molten lead burns the place of the fistula and heals it with a wonderful healing.
But if the fistula is healed with what we have said about cautery and treatment, it is good. And if not, then it is necessary to enlarge the nasal passage and redirect the fistula to the course of the nose, according to what will come to its own proper place. ➤ ➤
To Cauterize Fissures of the Lips
Often there are fissures on the lips, which are called "hairs," and especially on the lips of children.
Therefore, when you are treating these fissures with what we said about the division of diseases, and it does not help, then prepare a small cautery blade like this one.
And let its concavity be according to the sharpness of the blade.
Then quickly place the heated one on these fissures until the cautery reaches the depth of the fissure.
Then treat it with cerate until it heals.
To Cauterize a Fistula of the Mouth
When an abscess occurs at the root of the gum, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth: then it produces pus and bursts: after that it becomes chronic and runs with pus, and a fistula forms: then you treat it, and it does not help in that case, then you must heat the cautery according to the size that fits into the fistula. ething is that if there is a fissure on the lip of a child, you should be careful not to burn too much of the surrounding flesh, because the child's flesh is soft and tender and easily burns. Then insert the heated one into the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand until the heated iron reaches its depth and end; do this once or twice.
Then treat it afterwards with what we said about treatment until it heals. ething is that if there is a fissure on the lip of a child, you should be careful not to burn too much of the surrounding flesh, because the child's flesh is soft and tender and easily burns.
If the pus drains away and it heals, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to expose the place and remove the necrotic flesh according to what will be said in its chapter.
"On the Method of Cauterizing Soft Gums and Teeth
When the gums are softened due to moisture and the teeth are loose, and after treating them with medicines they do not improve, then place the patient's head on your lap.
Then, take a cautery tool whose form will be described later, and place the cannula over the tooth. Quickly introduce the burning cautery into it, and hold your hand for a moment until the patient feels the heat of the fire has reached the root of the tooth.
And lift your hand; then repeat the cautery several times according to your will.
Then the patient should fill his mouth with salt water and hold it for an hour, then spit it out.
For a loose tooth is made firm, a softened gum is tightened, and the corrupted moisture is dried.
"On the Method of Cauterizing for Toothache
When toothache is caused by coldness, whether the cold is within the tooth itself or in a worm, and treatment with medicines does not help, then there are two ways to apply cautery to it: either cautery with butter or cautery with fire.
The method of cautery with butter is as follows: take fresh cow's butter and boil it in an iron ladle or a bronze bowl. Then take a piece of cotton and wrap it around the end of a probe. 》 Then dip the cotton in the boiled butter and quickly place it on the aching tooth, holding it until it cools down; then repeat this several times until the heat of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, dip wool or cotton in cold butter and place it on the aching tooth; then place a burning iron on it until the fire reaches the depth of the tooth's cavity.
"The cauterization of it with fire is performed by placing a tube of air or a tube of iron. "And there should be something thick in the body, so that the sharpness of the fire does not reach the mouth of the wound.
"Then take a cautery of fire and place it on that tooth until the cautery cools.
"Do this several times, for the pain will be removed either on that same day or another day.
"And it is necessary for the patient to fill his mouth with good butter and hold it for one hour; then he should spit it out.
"And this is the form of the cautery.
"Cauterize with whatever sharp end is possible; and this is the shape of the tube.
"On the method of cauterizing in cases of thrush.
"When thrush is caused by phlegm and cold moisture and does not respond to treatment with medicines, and you wish to quickly hasten their digestion; then take a hollow cautery of fire, the shape of which is this.
"Having two open ends, so that the smoke may escape from one end; and place it ignited on the swelling once or twice if needed, until it reaches the depth of the swelling.
"But if the swelling is small, then place the cautery according to the size of the swelling.
"Then leave it for three days, and place a piece of cotton soaked in butter on it until what the fire has burned is removed.
"Then treat it with tooth salve until it heals to the shape of a tube.
"On the method of cauterizing hoarseness and constriction of breath.
When moistness overcomes the bronchial tube, especially when it is with cold disposition, then the sick person should be first evacuated with purgative medicines.
Then burn the patient on the neck at the root of the throat in a depressed place; and be careful not to reach the throat with the cautery, nor the skin, except for something of it.
Then burn the patient with another cautery at the neck joint in the last vertebra of the collarbone; and let the cautery be small according to the previously mentioned method.
Then treat the patient with what has been mentioned until he is healed.
On how to burn in lung diseases and coughs.
When cough and lung disease are from cold moistness, and the patient has no fever or phthisis (consumption), and the disease is not chronic, then burn the patient with two cauteries above the collarbone in depressed, mild, empty places. And with another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two breasts; and let the cautery be like a reed according to the previous method.
And if you wish to burn by pricking with a cautery called the Point, whose shape has been mentioned for pricking ear pain; and let the pricks be up to thirty in number, almost to the others.
Then treat him with what has been mentioned until he is cured.
And now let the cautery have three branches: according to this shape. Why is the burning alleviated when you do with it in one application the work of three cauteries? >()
Chapter 27.
When the head is dislocated because of humors and does not reset within an hour after its dislocation, until it becomes habitual for it to return, then it should be reduced from a slight movement that occurs as we have already testified about that; then you should reduce the dislocation first. Then the patient is turned onto their back, or onto their healthy side. Then lift up the skin which is on the inner part of the thigh with your left hand fingers and if the joint is dislocated towards the inside.
Then take a cautery with two prongs. Whose form is this:
Then cauterize the skin until it penetrates through to the other side, and a figure of four cauteries will appear.
And sometimes the cautery is done with a three-pronged cautery, which results in a figure of six cauteries; and these prongs are according to the fineness of the thread.
And this is the form of the three-pronged cautery.
And sometimes an additional one is added to this method, making eight cauteries in total.
Then place crushed garlic mixed with salt on the cautery. Then make the patient lie still so that the limb is not moved at any time until it becomes stronger.
And if the dislocation is towards the upper part, which rarely happens, then cauterize it on the shoulder with a nail-shaped cautery or by making multiple punctures with many cauteries.
For the joint is strengthened and the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.  />
¶ On the method of cauterizing the stomach.
When cold and excessive moisture affect the stomach, to the point of drawing it away from its natural temperament, and produce catarrh in it, and when the repeated methods of treatment prove ineffective, then the patient must be turned onto their back, extending their legs and hands. Then cauterize with three cauteries: a shell-shaped cautery the size of one finger joint on the chest, along with a nail-shaped cautery, and two more cauteries below, one on each side of the first cautery, until a triangular figure appears. And extend between both so that they do not join when making pus.
And the depth of the cautery should be two-thirds the thickness of the skin.
And let the figure of the cauteries be according to this form without addition: and if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form: and let the cautery by which this is done be one, according to the form of a circle according to this form.
And the stomach is cauterized by pricking it with this cautery: and it is as if you mark on the stomach a point according to the quantity that you wish with encaustic: then cauterize it with the point cautery; then treat it with the treatment mentioned until it heals.
¶ On the method of cauterizing cold spleen.
When pain occurs in the spleen from cold and moisture, or from excessive flatulence, until it excretes its superfluous excretion according to its natural constitution, and the patient is treated with what we have said, but does not improve: then it is necessary that the patient be turned onto their back, and mark three cauteries with encaustic in this form and size below the hypochondrium, where the arm reaches: and let the space between each cautery be according to the thickness of a finger; and let the cautery be straight according to the length of the body. And do not press too hard with your hand on the cautery.
And let the quantity that is burned be half the thickness of the skin, without addition: and let the patient stand on their feet.
If, however, the patient is unable to stand, then let them lie down with their legs extended and their arms raised.
This is the form of the cautery.
And you may indeed be able to cauterize this cautery with a scalpel cautery when you have skill and knowledge in the art.
And beware not to proceed too far in cauterization, so that the thickness of the whole skin is burned, which burns the whole body and reaches the intestines; for there the skin is thin, know this.
On the method of cauterizing liver abscesses.
When the abscess bursts and you want to know whether it is in the flesh of the liver or its membrane, then if it is in the flesh of the liver, a pain and weight without sharpness comes upon the patient; but if it is in the membrane of the liver, along with the pain there is severe sharpness. And you see that his physicians have been tired out by his treatment.
Therefore, the patient should lie on his back. Then mark the site of the abscess with a cautery; then heat the cautery which resembles a ray. And this is its shape. And burn with it once until the whole skin is burned and reaches the abscess, until all the pus comes out; then treat him with the treatment of bursts until he heals.
And it is not appropriate for someone to use this kind of cautery unless his study in the art of medicine has been prolonged and through whose hands these diseases have often passed with experience; then indeed he may dare to perform such an operation.
But to leave it alone is better in my opinion.
¶ On the method of cauterizing pleurisy.
The ancients said: for cold pleurisy, use a cautery with the roots of Aristolochia in this manner. eben And it is done by taking from the dried roots of Aristolochia a root longer than the others that can be found there, and let its thickness be like that of a finger. Then immerse it in oil and light it on fire. Then cauterize with one cautery between the continuation of the furcula and the neck, and with two small cauteries slanting downwards towards that which is under the beard.
And with two more cauteries slanting downwards towards the back between the fifth and sixth ribs; and one cautery in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. And three more cauteries from behind: one between the two scapulae; and two below that cautery which is between the two scapulae.
And it is not necessary to press the hand with the cautery, but rather let it be in plain sight, giving off its scent on the skin.
And some ancient authorities have said that there are men who use a cautery of iron like a needle, and they heat it and insert it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess, and pus comes out, as we have said concerning the hepatic abscess.
But in this perforation with the cautery there is fear that either the patient dies immediately, or a fistula results which cannot be healed.
§ On Cauterizing the Spleen Chapter XXXII.
When you are treating an illness of the spleen, according to what we have said about the division of diseases and your treatment is not effective, then there are three ways to cauterize it, all of which are correct.
The first is to make three or four cauteries in a line along the length of the spleen, following the shape of the liver cauteries whose figure we have described earlier.
And between each cautery there should be the thickness of a finger or a little more or less.
And the method of cauterizing should be as we have described for the liver cautery, equally so.
And do not press down with the cautery, and let the patient be lying on their back.
And another method of cauterization is as follows: Heat the cautery that has two prongs, which we have mentioned in the chapter on dislocation of the arm; and raise the skin that lies directly over the spleen, where the patient's left elbow reaches; and let your raising of the skin be according to the width of the body, so that the cauteries fall along the length of the body.
Then introduce the two red-hot prongs until you pierce through the skin from the other side; then withdraw the cautery. Thus, four cauteries are made.
And if you wish to cauterize with another cautery that has three prongs.
Then take care of the cautery after you have released it to discharge pus for many days, for it is more beneficial than any other previous treatment.
On the Method of Cauterizing for Hydrops.
The cautery does not work in hydrops except when used on the affected area itself. />
When you treat a hydroptic patient with the treatment methods mentioned in the division, and the treatment does not take effect, then it is necessary to cauterize him four times around the navel, and once on the stomach, and once on the liver, and once on the spleen, and twice on the back between the shoulders, and one directly over the chest, and another directly over the stomach. And let the depth of the cautery be close to the thickness of the skin.  />
Then leave the cautery open so that it may discharge pus for a long time.
And do not evacuate the patient from treatment after the cautery, for two benefits are added to him: and healing will hasten to him with the help of God.
The form of the caustic used to burn the stomach should be like a key; and that used for burning the back should be like an olive leaf, as described above.
On the method of cauterizing the feet and legs.
When they become swollen in a dropsical patient and fill with yellowish water, you should cauterize above the sole of the foot, which is between the auricular and annular bones; and lift up your hand with the caustic, and do not twist it; then lift up your hand, and do not press it at all.
For the yellowish water will ooze out, and let the caustic be of this shape.
Then make two caustics on each of the two legs, and let the caustic be with a knife-shaped tip; and let the caustic be as long as the leg, one below the knee and the other lower than that, about halfway down the leg. And make two caustics on each hip. And leave the caustic open without treatment for a long time, so that some water may ooze out from it; then treat it along with the others we have mentioned.
On the method of cauterizing to relieve abdominal pain.
Chapter XXXV.
When there is abdominal pain due to cold and moisture, which weakens the retentive and digestive powers in the stomach and intestines; and it is treated with remedies but does not heal; and you see that the patient can tolerate a strong caustic, then cauterize him strongly on his stomach, as described before for the method of cauterizing the stomach with a circular caustic, and four subtle caustics around the navel, with a subtle key-shaped caustic; and a large caustic over the groin above the testicles, or two caustics.
And if you see abundant moisture and the patient tolerates it, then cauterize with a hot iron over the comb and a hot iron over each eye; and perhaps add two small cauteries near the great vein.
For indeed is a treatment that is successful, whose benefit does not go astray.
¶ On the Method of Cauterizing Hemorrhoids.
Chapter XXXVI.
When there are many old hemorrhoids in the anus, or just one, from thick, cold humors, or corrupt humidity, and they are treated as we have said in division, but no cure is effective; then cauterize with three hot irons on the lower back of the spine under the almieda briefly in a triangular shape, and with one hot iron under the navel about two finger-widths.
And if you think that his stomach is chilled and he cannot digest food, and you see his face swollen; then cauterize him with a large hot iron on the stomach as before, and with one on his liver, another on his spleen, together with a clavicle cautery. Leave the cautery open for some time, then treat him until he is cured.
Chapter XXXVII.
When you cut out a hemorrhoid, then heat a hot iron that resembles a ray. Then insert the glowing iron into the cut hemorrhoid, and with your hand press until the hot iron reaches the opening of the vein from which the blood flows; do this once or twice.
If therefore the hemorrhoids are many, then cauterize each one with a hot iron as we have narrated. xspace Then treat them with that which is beneficial for them from the ointments until they are healed.
And if you cauterize him with a large cautery over the cataract, it is more effective for treatment.
On the method of cauterizing an anal fistula.
Chapter XXXVIII.
When the patient does not comply with the incision and operation that we have described in its place, and is terrified by it, perhaps he will be cured with a cautery.
Therefore, when someone has an anal fistula and it becomes chronic, pus runs from it, along with corrupting moisture. It is more appropriate, therefore, to probe it with a fine probe. Then recognize its depth with the probe.
Then heat the cautery, which is similar to a ray [of light]. Then introduce the heated cautery into the fistula itself and the amount of depth that the probe entered.
And repeat the cautery on it until all those corrupt bodies are burnt away, once, or twice, or three times, according to your necessity.
And beware of burning the nerve, if it is there, or a large vein; or if the fistula extends to the bladder body, or the intestine body, then beware of all these places. ︎
And do not do this unless the fistula is in a fleshy place; and know that it does not penetrate deeply.
Then care for the place until it heals.
But if the place seals up and matter separates from it, and it remains like this for a long time; then know that it has already been completely healed.
And if matter does not separate from it, then know that it is deep-seated, or there is a corrupt opening within it, or something like this; whose reminder will come in its place.
On the method of cauterizing the kidneys.
When pain occurs in the kidneys due to cold or excessive flatulence, and it lessens because of this weakness of the patient, then you should cauterize him above the almenthenem on the kidneys themselves, with a cautery over each kidney with a small cautery, which comes before the remembrance.
And perhaps we will cauterize him a second time in that same place. Why will three lines appear? Therefore, they will be more effective in the end.
§ On the method of cauterizing the bladder.
When there is weakness and softening of the bladder from cold and moisture, to the point that the patient cannot hold urine, then you should cauterize him on the lower part of the abdomen over the bladder where the hairs of the pubis begin, with a cautery from the right side of the abdomen and another from the left. And let the length of this cauterization be according to the width of the thumb joint; and you should cauterize him with a lower back cautery or with two if you need them; and it should be as the small cautery comes before.
§ On the method of cauterizing the uterus.
When there is cold and moisture in the uterus, which prevents impregnation and corrupts its menses, delaying their onset, and causing pain during their arrival, then it should be cauterized with three cauteries around the navel as we have said for the bladder, and with a cautery over the alcatim on the lower back, or with two if necessary; and let the cautery be small.
§ On the method of cauterizing the ankle in dislocation.
When mucous humors flow to the ankle and cause it to leave its place; and the sign of this is that one leg is longer than the other when compared, and the place of dislocation is found empty.
It is therefore necessary to cauterize the patient over a box of Anchae with a similar cautery circle. After marking it with wax around the box as it turns, so that the box itself falls into the middle of the circle.
If this cautery is not available to you, then use three cauteries: a large olive-oil cautery and make the depth of the cautery according to the thickness of the entire skin.
Then care for it until it heals.
§ On Cauterizing for Sciatica
When pain occurs in the bladder and its cause is cold and moisture, and the patient is treated with what we have said in the division of humors, but it does not help and the disease persists, then you must free the patient from thick humors with stinking pills or artificial pills and similar ones. Then cauterize him.
And the method of cautery is according to two methods: either a cautery with drying medicines or a cautery with fire. xspace
A cautery with fire is done in many ways.
One of these methods is to cauterize over the bladder itself with three triangular cauteries in this shape. ️ And make them of good or bad depth. And let the space between each cautery be the size of a thick finger, and let the cautery be made with olive oil.
Sometimes, however, the cautery is done in the middle over the head of the bladder itself. ️ ️ ️ Why are there four cauteries?
And if you wish to cauterize with a circle, whose form has been described for the cauterization of bladder dislocation, do so with one, so that the circle contains the entire bladder.
"And burn the thickness of the entire skin.
This is the method of cautery for sciatica when the pain clings to the hip itself and does not extend to the thigh and leg.
But if it extends to the thigh and leg, then cauterize with two cauteries over the hip, on the spot where the patient indicates that the pain is, and your cautery four fingerbreadths towards the tendon briefly; and let the cautery be knife-like.
And let the depth of the cautery be according to the thickness of the skin.
But if the patient indicates that the pain extends almost to the toes of the foot, then cauterize there where he indicates with a point or three, or four, or more, as needed.
And if the patient indicates that the pain is under the knee towards the leg, then cauterize there with one knife-like cautery.
And beware in all your cautery that you do not go with the cautery to the point of burning a large nerve or artery and thereby draw a harmful disease or contraction upon the patient.
And indeed I myself have seen one and another of those who cauterized over the tendon and carried the cautery to completion, and their leg swelled up until a tumor reached the foot and the whole thing burst, and the entire foot was corrupted; then came an opening in the belly, and death after that.
But if the pain is in two parts at the same time, cauterize each one according to this manner.
And some wise men said in the cautery of the hip, whose method this is. Make a similar awl from iron, whose diameter is half the width of a palm; and at its opening let there be according to the thickness of an almond, or slightly less; and inside that awl let there be a third awl.
And let there be a space between each samium equal to the thickness of the thumb; and let the samia be open on both sides; and let their height be like that of a knot, or two knots; and make for them a handle from iron, well fitted into the samia.
Then it should be heated in the fire until it turns red and sparks fly out; then it should be placed on a weak patient's side, above the healthy part of the chest. Therefore, cauterize him with three round cauteries at once.
Then leave him for three days. Afterwards, apply plasters with butter; and let the wound remain open for many days. Then treat him with ointment until he is healed.
Albucasis said: "O my son, we have used this kind of cautery little because of the frightening appearance of it; and also, because few can bear its application.
However, for him who endures, it is among the good cauteries, and he who finds a place for it will be successful with it.
The cautery is also made with adherent medicines, such that you should make two samia having a perforated armilla, into which descends the pin of its door, either from bronze or iron, as long as the wall; whose height should be two knots, or similar to them.  />
And let the space between the two be the thickness of a finger; and let them be open below and above; and let them contain each other in this manner.
Then place it on the chest of a weak patient lying on the healthy side. And press your hand firmly against the chest. Then pour between the two samia warm water which has been heated a little by fire, and hold it for an hour; and let the patient endure its burning and its scorching, for he will find the burning like fire until the burning ceases.
Then lift your hand with the instrument and wash away all the hot water from the wound with sweet water; then leave it alone for three days.
And put butter on it until the blackness of the burn is removed; and leave it for some days, and pus will flow from it. For it is most helpful in treatment.
Then care for it with ointments until it heals.
But if the pain extends to the hip or thigh, make for him a bath in which there is water, as you did for the wound, in the same way.
And this is the method of hot water; and I have already written it down in the chapter on rectifying medicines. Take soda and unslaked lime in equal parts; grind both of them finely and put them in a new pot whose bottom is pierced with one small hole through which the liquid can pass, and under the bottom of the pot place another glass pot, and pour over the soda and lime sweet water so that it covers both by a finger's width; then press them firmly with your hand; and leave the pot until the sharp water descends into the lower part of the glass pot.
Then collect all that water and pour it over another lime; and strain it through a cloth until it is clear.
For then it will be very strong, which is used in many operations of medicine and in the cautery of other members. Because it performs the action of fire itself.
And among the medicines that are used to cauterize wounds, there is also terebinth resin and almond oil and lime mixed with soap.
And indeed Galen reported the cure of a certain ancient man, by which he was cured of pain in his wound and sciatic vein; and he praised it greatly. 》 And he said that no other treatment was needed, and that he was cured after one application until he reported that perhaps he had entered a bath house and came out of it already healthy.
And take it from a green sebet plant: and if you cannot find it fresh, take the dried kind, recently harvested. Grind it very finely with some fat, and place it on the ulcer where there is pain, either on the leg or in the hip. Bind it, and leave it on for three hours, or however long the patient feels relief from the burning sensation. Then introduce him to a bath.
When his body becomes sweaty, place him on a stool. For the pain subsides and he is cured.
And know that no one should use cautery with these medicines unless after purging the body.
And Dioscorides said that goat dung, when used to cauterize the sciatic vein, helps it: and this is how you make the cautery. Take wool and soak it in old oil, and place it on the deep place that is between the thumb of the foot and the ankle bone, which is closer to the ankle bone.
Then take dry goat dung and burn it in a fire until it becomes charcoal. ›
Then place the charcoal on the wool and leave it until it goes out. Then repeat that process. Do not cease to do this until the sensation reaches the ulcer and the pain subsides.
And this method of cautery is called the goat dung cautery.
¶ On the Cautery for Back Pain
Sometimes back pain occurs due to many causes, such as injury, a blow, or excessive purging, and similar things, from the infusion of cold, wet matter. And indeed, cautery is only indicated in this particular case, which is caused by the infusion of cold matter.
It is therefore necessary after the evacuation of the patient with foul-smelling pills and similar ones that three lines be made on the back where it hurts, according to the width of the almeidat itself, after marking with a cautery in each line five or more burns, as many as come from the strength of the patient's tolerance. And let the cauterization be done with a cautery point.
And if you wish, cauterize with three or four cauteries using the middle of a nail-shaped cautery according to this method.
On the method of cauterizing an incipient hump.
This illness often happens to small children.
And the sign of its onset in children is that a stricture occurs in their breath as they rise and move, and it is found in the last vertebrae of the back and in its nodes, which have already begun to protrude above the other vertebrae.
When you see it and wish to do this, then cauterize with a circular cautery according to this method.
And let the cautery take hold of each part of the vertebrae equally. If you wish to cauterize around the vertebra with a point cautery, make two or three lines and let the points be close together.
Then care for the place until it heals with what we have said.
And beware of applying a cautery to a hump caused by a nerve spasm.
On the method of cauterizing gout and joint pains.
When the pains of the joints are from cold humors that flow into any part of the body, then when these pains occur in the feet, according to the custom of physicians, they properly name it gout.  ()
When treating gout caused by cold with remedies and the pain is not removed, then a cautery will remove them.
And it should be that he is cauterized after purging around the joint of the foot with many cauteries; and let the cautery be olive oil-based.
And if you need to prick on the surface of the foot, then do it with a small pricking iron. If the pain ascends to the knees or other joints, and this often happens, then cauterize him on every knee with three or four cauteries from all sides, using the same clavile iron.
But if you need more of this cautery, then cauterize him again. And do not plunge your hand with the cautery; rather let it be about as thick as the skin.
But if the pain ascends to the knees and back, then administer what we said about the cautery in its own chapter.
But if the pain is only in the hands, then prick around the joints as two lines revolve.
But if any pain remains in the fingers, then prick them on every joint with a single prick, and also on the palm of the hand.
But if after days the pain ascends to the elbows or shoulders, then cauterize both from all sides.
And do not purge the patient from a good diet and from taking medication. For if a good regimen is followed and the phlegm is purged, he will be healed with God's help by means of this cautery.
¶ On the method of cauterizing ruptures.
When a rupture occurs in the groin and the intestine or scrotum descends to the testicle, and this is an urgent case, then it is necessary that you instruct the patient to abstain from food for that day. And let him use laxatives so that his stool may pass from his belly.
Then let him sit between your hands on his back; and instruct him to hold his breath until it comes out, or a turd appears, or the intestine.
Then reduce him with your fingers, and mark the place of the rupture above the anus with a cautery, with a mark whose end is like half a circle towards the upper part of the body.
Then apply fire to the cautery until pus comes out and it throws off scabs. Then reduce the intestine or turd back to its natural place. Then have the assistant place his hand over the site to prevent the intestine from exiting; and you have now opened between the patient's thighs and placed a pillow underneath, and another servant on his legs, and another on his chest who holds his hands.
Then place the cautery over that mark, with your hand holding the cautery upright. And hold him until you reach his mouth with it; or repeat the process with another if you have not reached the mouth on the first try.
And be mindful of the exit of the intestine during your cautery, lest you burn it and cause death or great harm to the patient through it.
And know that when you do not reach the mouth with the cautery, your work is in vain.
And it is necessary for the cautery of infants to be fine, according to their measure.
Then care for him with other ointments until he is healed.
And let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound closes.
And it is necessary that you provide his food during the time of his treatment, so that it may soften his belly; so that the intestine does not come out at the attempt or discharge.  />
Then, when he wants to get up after forty days, give him a well-made bandage and let him keep it for another forty days.
And let him be kept from labor, and from filling his stomach with food and drink, and from loud voices.
For when he follows this treatment, he is healed by a complete cure.
And I will describe the treatment of hernias with incisions in its own chapter.
But when hernias occur in the rest of the abdomen and are beginning and you wish that they not increase, then cauterize his hernia with a round cautery according to its size: and let what is burnt be one-third of it. ))) Then treat him as we have said, and there will be no increase.
And some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with a triangular cautery in this shape.
After it is marked with the cautery, and a line is placed which is along its width on the upper side of the hernia, and another line below it. And place your hand in the middle with a nail-shaped cautery.
But the first cautery is easier and better. ))) )))
¶ On the method of cauterizing for pains from a fall or blow.
Chapter 48.
When there is pain in certain members from a fall or blow, and the pain persists for a long time, and medicine does not help it, then it must be cauterized with a point-shaped cautery. ))) ))) )))
And let the cautery be of every member according to its size and thinness and weakness and strength, and where the blow or pain is from that. ))) ))) ))) )))
If he is healed from the first cautery, that is good. ))) ))) ))) ))) ))) ))) "If not, then repeat on that same cautery.
Because it is the custom of these pains to pass from one member to the next adjacent one. Therefore you should follow them with a cautery until the patient is healed.
§ On the manner of cauterizing in leprosy.
Sometimes lepers are greatly helped by cautery. And especially the kind of leprosy that comes from the corruption of phlegm and black bile. When you wish to cauterize it, be mindful of this.
If the leprosy is in its beginning stage and you have treated it with what we mentioned in the division, and it does not descend or stop; and you fear for the patient that corruption may overcome his entire complexion; then cauterize him on the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the head, a second below it towards the forehead at the hairline, two above each temple, and one behind on the nape of the neck.
And finally, place your hand with the cautery briefly on it, so that it makes a small impression on the skin and causes the scabs to detach from it; this will relieve the exhalation of thick vapors from it. Also cauterize the spleen itself as we have previously described.
But if the leprosy has already spread over the patient and is clearly visible; then you must cauterize with these cauteries that we have mentioned on the head, and one cautery on the tip of the nose, and two cauteries on each cheek, and two on each side of the neck, and six on each side of the back, and a large one on the scrotum at the root of the penis and one above it in the bellybutton; and two on each shoulder blade, that is, with one on each shoulder blade and two on each knee: one on each knee and two on each elbow, and two on each wrist, and two on each side of his chest. And cauterize him on every joint among the joints of the fingers of both his hands and feet; and cauterize on each heel of his feet and on each palm of his hands.  />
And beware of the nerves that are on the back of the heel, lest you burn them.
And sometimes it is cauterized with a hot iron over the pubic bone, and another over the xiphoid process of the sternum, and another over the liver.
And know that the more you apply the hot iron, it is more beneficial and effective.
And know that the sick person does not feel pain from the hot iron as much as a healthy person would, because their body is already numb.
And the hot irons should be made according to size and shape for different limbs and joints, as has been mentioned in the types of surgical instruments.
Then treat the wounds with a poultice made from ground herbs and honey, and continue other treatments until it heals.
On the Method of Cauterizing When Someone is Insensible.
When a limb becomes insensible and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, but does not heal, then cauterize the insensible limb with hot irons, according to the size or shape of the limb.
And let your hot iron penetrate slightly into the thickness of the skin. Then treat it with ointment until it heals.
And sometimes it is cauterized for the numbness that occurs in the hand or foot, at the spine of the back near where the nerves that move that limb emerge; and the numbness will be removed.
But do not attempt this unless you are knowledgeable in the dissection of limbs and the exit points of the nerves that move the body.
Book Fifty-One
When a whitlow becomes old and nothing helps it from the healing arts, then cauterize it slightly with a deep hot iron according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and its color changes.
Then care for it with herb flour and lentils with rose oil, and arnoglossa leaves, and dove's blood, and swallow's blood: let there be an equal part of each. Let all these be mixed together and smeared on a cloth, and adhere to the place until it heals.
On the method of cauterizing in cancer.
When the cancer is beginning and you wish to stop it, then cauterize it with a circular cautery around its circumference, as if turning [a wheel].
However, the wise have said that it should be cauterized with the final cautery in the middle.
But this does not seem right to me, because I fear that it will cause an ulceration; and indeed I have seen this happen many times.
And it is more appropriate to cauterize around its circumference with a circle, as we have said, or with many cauteries.
On the method of cauterizing in abscesses.
When someone has an abscess and it is delayed in ripening, either because of the excess humour causing it, or because of the weakness of the patient when they are elderly and have little blood, or because of the time and the desire to hasten the ripening of the abscess, then cauterize around its circumference with many small puncturing cauteries. Then leave it alone. For it will hasten in ripening on its own.
But if you wish to pierce it with a cautery, then heat the cautery, which has this form: ¶ [A drawing of the cautery may be included here.]
And place it in the middle of the abscess, until it penetrates the skin. Let the cautery be from the weakest patient, so that the course of pus may be facilitated.
Then care for it until it heals.
About the method of cauterizing in malignant ulcers.
Chapter 46.
The ulcer is nothing but corruption moving through the limb, and it eats away at that limb, just as fire consumes dry wood.
Therefore, if you see an ulcer in a place that can bear cautery with fire, then burn it much with fire, both small and large cauteries, according to what is suitable for the place where the ulcer is.
Then cauterize it on all sides until you have completely removed all the corruption and nothing of it remains at all.
Then leave it for three days, and place ground sulfur mixed with oil on the cauterized places, until all the scabs are removed and all corruption is eliminated.
Then treat it with flesh-generating ointments.
Therefore, if you see that after three days healthy flesh is born, in which there is no corruption, it is good. ️
And if not: then repeat the cautery on whatever remains from the corrupted places.
And the ulcer should be treated at times with sharp medicine. ️ For it arises in the place of the cautery.
However, cautery with fire is of swifter help; and I have already spoken of its cauterization with sharp medicine in the division; therefore take it there when you need it.
¶ About the method of cauterizing in nails and warts.
Chapter 50.
Many times this illness occurs in the lower parts of the feet; and it is a thick, rough substance that injures the foot.
And there are two types of cautery in them: cautery with fire, and cautery with hot water.
As for the one with fire, use a concave cautery like a vulture's feather, made of iron according to the size that can contain the nail from all sides; and let it have thin edges. ️ ️ ️
Then place the heated instrument on the nail. Then rotate the hand with the cautery around the nail until the cautery reaches the depth of the nail, and leave it for three days until it begins to emit pus. Then apply a plaster with crushed wild mallows mixed with salt, and leave the plaster on it overnight. It will be uprooted from its roots.
Then care for the place with a flesh-generating ointment until it heals.
But if they do not convert and often occur on the surface of the body, especially in the hands and feet, then administer the cautery with hot water. And it is that you take a tube made of bronze, or iron, or from a vulture's feather, and place it on the nail, or althelul. Then pour a small amount of hot water into the tube; hold your hand and rotate it with some pressure for a short while, so that the edge of the tube is impressed on the root of the nail, and the hot water finds its way to the depth, to the root of the nail; and let the patient wait for an hour over the biting of the hot water.
Then leave it, for the nail will be uprooted with its roots.
Do this one after another until you have treated all those that are on the body.
Then care for them after they have been uprooted with that which generates flesh from ointments.
¶ On the method of cauterizing in tremors.
When trembling occurs to someone from cold in the nerves, or from tertian fever, or something else, then it is necessary that you cauterize him with four or five cauteries on the vertebrae of the back, and between every vertebra a cautery, and on his chest a cautery, and on his stomach a cautery.
The tremor quiets with oil cautery, and health quickly returns from cold illness.
On the manner of cauterizing according to Albathar.
Chapter 57.
Sometimes Albathar expels foul things from the body, that is, pustules which are formed from coarse corrupt matter.
Therefore, as soon as they appear, they should be cauterized with a fine cautery made of myrtle wood, the end of which is set on fire. Or with the root of long aristolochia. Or with a lentil-shaped cautery. ︎
And sometimes they are cauterized with the adenoma at the beginning of its expulsion in this manner, and they do not increase; and the excess causing them is broken up, and they heal from it.
However, that should be done after evacuation with bloodletting.
On the manner of cauterizing a wound to stop bleeding from an artery.
It often happens that there is bleeding from an artery cut in a wound, which occurs externally or during the incision of an aposteme, or of a member's cautery, and similar to these; and it is difficult to cut it off.
Therefore, when this happens to someone, quickly bring your hand to the opening of the artery and place your index finger on it. And press it hard until the blood is blocked under your finger and nothing comes out of it.
Then put a small oil cautery and several large ones into the fire, and blow on them until they are very hot. ︎ ︎
Then take one of them, either small or large, according to the wound and the place where the artery is cut, and put the cautery on the vein itself after you quickly remove your finger; and hold the cautery until the bleeding stops.
