Chapter LXIV.
§ On the care of the hands, which is with the tendons.
The tendons are a swelling wrapped in some wrapping, similar to a bunch of grapes, with the softening of the testicles; and it becomes difficult for the patient to move, exercise, or walk.
And in the treatment of this disease, there is fear from the memory of what preceded it.
Indeed, we must say that the operation on it should be done according to what was first done.
I say, therefore, that you should have the patient sit on a raised seat. Then push the scrotum downwards. Then hold the skin of the scrotum with your fingers, together with the vessels that are close to the penis; and let another assistant hold it and stretch it strongly.
Then cut with a broad, sharp scalpel across the vessels until the vessels are exposed.
Then peel it from all sides, as we have told you in the removal of the temporal arteries. ›
Then pierce it with a needle that has two threads, and tie the thread first at the place where the tendons come together; and tie it again at their end. › › Then cut it with a straight cut along the length of the body, and remove what has accumulated from foul, corrupted moisture.
Then treat the wound with the treatment of other wounds, so that there will be strength to generate pus, until the vessels that nourish one of the testicles fall away. For it is not a harm in this way.
But if the tendons are affected in all the vessels, then it is necessary to remove the testicles with the vessels; so that the egg may not be deprived of nourishment because of the incision, and waste away or dry up, and there will be no benefit from them.
Chapter 65.
The care of the rectum and intestines.
The outcome of this rectal issue is from a cut, which occurs in the scrotum extended over the abdomen at the groin from the navel.
Why do the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the testicles? And this rupture is either from the scrotum or its extension.
And these two types occur from many causes: either from a blow, or a jump, or a shout, or lifting a heavy object, and similar things.
And the sign, when it is from the extension of the scrotum. ‌ It is that it happens gradually over a long time, and does not happen suddenly: and there is an abscess of equal depth: because the scrotum compresses the intestine.
And the sign of it when it is from a cut in the scrotum, because at its beginning it causes a sudden and severe pain: and there is an abscess that appears near the surface of the skin: and this is due to the exit of the intestine and its course to the outside of the scrotum. ‌
And sometimes it exits with the intestine and the testicle: and this is called rectal intestine and testicle: and sometimes it happens with flatulence.
And sometimes feces runs into the intestine and is retained there: and with it is the destruction of the sick person: because it causes a severe pain, especially when pressed upon.
And in treating these types of illness with iron, there is fear: therefore one must be careful to avoid this error.
And the method of treatment is that you should instruct the patient to return the intestine by his own hand into the interior of his pelvis, if it is willing to return. ‌ ‌ Then he should be made to lie on his back between your hands: and lift his legs.
Then extend the skin that follows the skin upwards, and cut through the entire length of the scrotal skin. Then insert hooks into the two lips of the incision according to your need to open the incision with them; and let the incision be such that it is possible for an egg to emerge from it.
Then scrape away the peritoneum and what is beneath the skin of the testicles until you uncover the white, hard album on all sides. Then insert your index finger between the testicle and that white album which lies beneath the skin, and separate it from the membrane at the back of the egg.
Then move the skin of the testicles towards the inside with your right hand, and at the same time stretch the white album upwards with your left hand; and lift the egg with its membrane towards the incision; and instruct your assistant to lift the egg upwards; and you separate the adhesion behind after the separation is completed.
And search with your fingers to see if there is anything of the intestine twisted within the hard white membrane. If, however, you find anything, then push it down towards the abdomen.
Then take a needle with a thick thread made from ten threads of linen; and insert it at the bottom of the membrane, that is, the tunica, which lies beneath the skin following the incision; then cut the ends of the thread that protrude until four threads remain. Then arrange some of them over others in the shape of a cross; and tie with them that membrane which we have spoken of, since it is beneath the skin of the testicles, with a strong ligature, so that none of the vessels which nourish them may send anything to them; lest there occur from this a hot abscess. And place another ligature following the first ligature, more distant from it by two fingers. And after these two ligatures leave out from the scrotal sac, which is under the skin of the testicles, an amount equal to the size of a finger: and cut off the rest entirely following its roundness, and remove the testicle from it.
Then cut in the lower part of the skin of the testicles with a section from which blood and pus flow, as we have described in what precedes.
Then apply wool soaked in oil to the wound, and apply the ligature that we have described. And sometimes the white scrotal sac which we mentioned is cauterized after its incision, fearing a flow of blood. For often it happens. And leave the ligature until it falls off by itself.
But if its falling off is delayed, then let it be soaked in warm water; and place on it that which we have mentioned until it falls off.
Then treat the wound with the rest of the treatment for wounds until it is healed.
Chapter 66.
¶ Concerning the Swollen Anus.
In this case of swollen anus I have not seen anyone who dared to treat it with iron.  /> But if he wants to use iron, let him cauterize around the anus at the place where the inflammation is more intense; and let him cut through the skin with a lancet above the anus as much as the width of two fingers.  /> And then let him introduce a probe into the anus, and let it be long enough to reach from the upper part of the buttocks to the lower part of the scrotum.
And indeed the first [authorities] said that it is done just as we have described in the case of piles with a fleshy base. That is to say, after the incision sew up the skin beneath it with ease; then cut in the middle [of the inflammation], and treat afterwards with that which opens it, until the skin falls off: and treat the wound as we have said until it heals.  /> But there are those who want to cauterize around the anus at the place where the inflammation is more intense; and then let them cut through the skin with a lancet above the anus as much as the width of two fingers.  /> And then let them introduce a probe into the anus, and let it be long enough to reach from the upper part of the buttocks to the lower part of the scrotum; Chapter LXVII
"On ruptures that occur in the groin.
When a rupture occurs in the groin, as we have said, and the area swells and nothing from the intestines descends: if it does descend, it is little and returns in all hours; but if this condition is prolonged, a tear forms in the scrotum until the intestines descend into the scrotum.
This occurs due to the stretching of the scrotum in the groin, as we have said. Which is because the scrotum is stretched; then it softens and becomes swollen, and protrudes.
And its treatment is with cautery, as was told in its preceding account.
Sometimes it is treated with a knife in this manner: the patient should lie on his back between your hands. Then cut the area of the ruptured and swollen protrusion with a longitudinal incision, to a width of three fingers. ‌
Then tie the scrotum and its contents under the skin until the white scrotum that follows it is exposed.
Then take a bandage and place it over the protruding area of the scrotum, and press it deeply into the abdomen. ‌
Then if there are two protruding areas at the end of the bandage from the scrotum, and join one with the other using a stitch; then remove the end of the bandage.
And do not cut the scrotum at all, nor pull on the testicle or anything else, as I have taught you in the treatment of intestinal hernias.
Then treat it with wound care. When you cut the threads, clean it and close the wound until it heals. ‌ ‌
For the scrotum contracts and no swelling of the rupture occurs. ‌
And cautery is better in this place because it is closer to health.
Chapter 68
On the softening of the skin of the testicles.
The skin of the testicles is often softened in certain men, causing the flesh between them to become soft and their appearance to be disfigured.
Therefore it is necessary for the person who is asked to treat this condition to make the patient lie on his back and cut away all the softened skin down to the natural skin.
Then bring together the two lips with stitches; and if you wish, first remove any excess of the softened skin with three or four stitches, and make the stitching firm.
Then cut between the stitches.
Then treat it as you would other wounds until it heals and the threads fall out.
Chapter 69
§ On castration.
Know that castration is forbidden by our law and therefore it would be permissible for me not to mention it in this book of mine. And mentioning it is not necessary except for two reasons.
The first reason is so that a doctor may know about it when asked about it, and be able to treat someone who has undergone it.
The second reason is that we often need to castrate certain animals for our own benefit, such as rams, donkeys, and cats, and similar animals.
I say therefore that castration can be done in two ways.  Either by rubbing. Or by cutting and slicing.
In the method of rubbing, the way to do it is this: make the animal sit in hot water until its testicles soften and relax and hang down; then rub them with your hand until they dissolve and cannot be felt.   
"However, in castration by tearing and cutting, it is necessary to hold the animal and press its testicular skin with your left hand.
"Then tie the suspensory ligament, and cut above each testicle with one cut until two testicles come out. After skinning both, incise them after you have removed from the scrotum everything except the fine skin that is over the vessels.
"And this method of castration is better than that which is done by friction, because friction perhaps leaves something of the testicles, so that the animal desires copulation.
"Then care for the wound until it heals.
Chapter 70
"§ On caring for a hermaphrodite of two kinds.
"A hermaphrodite is made from men in two ways. "One way is that it appears in him following the space, or on the skin of the testicles, between the two testicles, in the form of a woman's vulva, with hair: and sometimes urine flows from what is on the skin of the testicles.
"In women, however, there is only one form, and it is like a woman's vulva on the pubis, just as if small male testicles were very prominent towards the outside: of which one is like the male penis, and two like two testicles.
"And the treatment for these three kinds—the two from men and the one from women—is that you should cut away the attached flesh until its impression is removed. "Then treat them with the care of other wounds.
"In the second type of men, from which urine exits and is on the skin of the testicles, there is no operation or care at all.
Chapter 71.
"§ On the cutting of excrescences and prominent flesh in women's vulvas.
Possibly the disease is added to a natural part, until it becomes ugly and unsightly: And sometimes it is greatly magnified in certain women, so much so that it expands as in men, and reaches the point of coition.
Therefore, you should hold the excess of the disease with your hand or with a hook, and cut it off: And do not proceed too far with the cutting, especially at the root of the deep part: So that there is no flow of blood.
Then care for it as you would a wound, until it heals.
But the flesh that is born is the flesh that grows in the orifice of the womb, until it fills it: And perhaps it goes out to the outside like a tail: And because of this some call it a 'tailed disease'. Therefore, you should cut it off as you would the wart, and care for it until it heals.
¶ About treating ulceration, which is an unperforated woman's genital sore.
Chapter 72.
An ulceration is when a woman has a sore that is not perforated, or has only a small hole. And it is either natural or accidental. ️
An accidental one is due to a previous disease: And this itself occurs either from added flesh that was born, or from sifach (a type of skin lesion), whether thin or thick. And it forms either in the depths of the womb, or on its sides, or on its upper part, or its lower part: And it prevents intercourse and impregnation, and childbirth, and perhaps even menstruation.
And recognition of it is done by the midwife's inspection, if there is an apparent swelling nearby.
If it is not visible, then seek it with your fingers or with a stick.
But if the swelling is from thin sifach and is near the two lips, then hasten and tear it off. ️ ️ ️
And it is like this: place small pills on the two lips.
Then place your fingers of both hands together, and let the woman be on her back with her legs spread apart. Then stretch both lips with strength until the fine sifak is torn open and the clitoris is exposed.
Then take wool and soak it in oil, and place it on the spot: and let the woman come every day, so that the place does not heal in another way.
But if the sifak is thick and dense: then it is necessary to cut it with a broad spatula similar to a myrtle leaf.
But if the clitoris is fleshy: then suspend it with hooks and cut it: and let there be with you medicines that stop the flow of blood without cauterization, such as acacia and dragon's blood, and egg white mixed with the white of an egg.
Then administer a large lead pipe so that the wound does not heal quickly, let her keep it for some days: and administer dry flax thread, then continue with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
And sometimes a birth of other flesh occurs in the womb: it is therefore necessary to cut them like this: as long as there is no cancerous tumor in the womb, for with a cancerous tumor that is in the womb, do not use iron at all.
Chapter LXXIII.
¶ On the care of hemorrhoids, and red bothers in women's wounds.
Hemorrhoids indeed are the opening of the veins' orifices, until much blood runs from them constantly. xspace
Therefore, when hemorrhoids are aggravated, they become tender; and I have already spoken of their division into species and signs in the section on them: and I will say here which of them receive treatment, and which do not.
I say, therefore, that hemorrhoids which are at the entrance of the womb and do not protrude: then there is no treatment for them with iron.
Those which are at the entrance of the womb and upon which one feels something are those that can be treated.
Therefore, it is necessary to introduce the woman into a cold house. Then, extend the perineum with scissors or with a rough cloth and cut them from their roots.
Then sprinkle on them a powder that stops bleeding from one of the wound-healing powders without cauterization: such as acacia, dragon's blood, sumac, and similar ones.
Then have her press her feet against the wall for an hour. Afterwards, place her in cold water.
If the bleeding persists: then have her sit in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate rinds, oak galls, and similar things.
Then take barley flour, mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a poultice with it on her back.
If the blood clots with it, that is good; if not, apply a cupping glass to her back and breasts without scarification.
Then take wool and soak it in the juice of tamarisk or the juice of sea lavender or the juice of oleander branches, that is, aglander, with Pontic wine, and apply it to the place.
When the abscess has quieted down, then treat the place with ointments until it heals.
Albarth, however, is reddish and resembles the heads of alfalfa, and has a rough appearance.
Therefore, it is necessary to cut away what appears from it, as I said about hemorrhoids equally: and treat it until it heals.
Chapter LXXIIII.
Perforation of the vagina that occurs in the womb.
There are many kinds of tumors that occur in the womb, such as cancer, stone tumors, ulcers, abscesses, carbuncles (i.e., herpes), abscesses with pustules, fistulas, hemorrhoids, fissures, and warm tumors.
And indeed, I have already mentioned all these diseases and their types, and their signs, and their treatments in the division. It is necessary for me to speak about warm tumors that occur in the womb, when it is among the tumors that collect pus, and I want to know how its opening with iron is done.
Therefore, you should consider. If the pain of the tumor is sharp at its onset with swelling, heat, and fever, and you see it become red; if sensation is lost over it, then do not hurry to open it; and treat it with what helps until the tumor matures, until the sharpness of the symptoms subsides.
Then it is necessary to make the woman sit on a seat that has two holes, and let her lean forward, or have her lie on her back, and gather her feet towards the lower part of the belly; and let her hips be spread apart, and let her place her arms under her knees, and bind each with an appropriate ligament.
Then let the midwife sit on the right side, and administer the instrument by which the opening of the womb is opened.
And when you want to administer this instrument, it is necessary that you pierce the deep part of the woman's womb with a rod; so that what enters from the instrument is no more than the depth of the womb, and does not harm the sick one.
If the instrument is deeper than necessary, then you should place cotton over the opening of the deep womb to prevent the entire instrument from entering into the deep womb; and it is necessary that a screw be placed on the side of the instrument, which runs along the instrument, so that it can hold the instrument and so that an assistant turns the screw until the deep womb opens.
When it appears at the orifice, and can be touched with the hand, and is soft and gentle, then you should cut it at its head with a broad knife.
When the wound is cleaned of pus, then you should place a linen cloth soaked in rose oil or green oil with some astringent properties over the wound, and apply pressure, and extract the incision from the deep womb.
And place externally over the womb and over the pubic bone a clean linen cloth soaked in water in which mulberries have been boiled.
Then it should be cleaned after two days with an appropriate ointment until it heals.
And sometimes the womb and the wound are washed with water and honey; then with water in which the root of lily or long aristolochia has been boiled; then return to using an ointment.
If the wound is hidden inside the womb, then you should avoid treating it with iron; rather, treat it with what we have mentioned in the section on division.
Chapter 70.
¶ The Art of Midwifery: How to Treat Live Embryos that Exit in an Abnormal Form.
The midwife must first know the natural form of childbirth.
From its signs, you will know that when a woman begins to feel pressure in her lower abdomen and desires fresh air, and what is above her womb is relieved, and the exit of the embryo hastens; then you should know that this birth is according to the natural form, and it exits with its head first, and the amnion either hangs from or follows the umbilical cord. ➤
When you see these signs, then it is necessary that his abdomen be pressed so that the child may quickly descend.
For when it descends upon its head, the afterbirth also descends with it and is purified from those excesses by a good cleansing.
But he who is born other than this way is unnatural and inauspicious.
For sometimes the fetus emerges feet first, and its body comes out before its head, or one of its feet or both of its hands, or only one foot; or it may come out head first with one hand; or perhaps the abdomen protrudes, and possibly turns over onto its neck, and other similar inauspicious positions. 》
Therefore it is necessary that the midwife be prudent and subtle in all these matters, and guard herself from error and deception. And I will show every figure of them, and what is its nature, and what it signifies, and how to handle it.
When the fetus emerges head first in its natural way of birth, and it becomes violent towards the woman, and her labor is difficult, and you see that her strength has already been weakened: then make her sit on a seat, or have women hold her; and fumigate her vulva with fenugreek boiled in water and with moist oils.
Then the midwife should insert a small spatula between her fingers, and she should probe with it to find the afterbirth, and she should cut it with her nail until the moisture flows from it; and she should press on the woman's abdomen until the fetus descends.
But if it does not descend, then it is necessary that the woman be given an enema of fenugreek mucilage with sesame oil.
After the enema, instruct her to press on herself; and make her sneeze with pepper, and hold her mouth and nose for one hour. The fetus will immediately emerge.
If two hands of the fetus come out first, it is necessary to gently bring them back little by little. If it does not comply at the entrance, then place the woman on a stool and lift her feet upwards; then shake the stool on the ground; and the woman should be held so that she does not fall from the shaking.
If the hands do not come out and the fetus dies, then cut them off and extract the rest of the fetus; and bind the hand with cloth, and extract it equally, for he will emerge.
The exit of the embryo is over his feet. When the fetus emerges over his feet, then it is necessary to push them upwards; then gradually turn the fetus; afterwards, even it out.
Then take one of its feet and extend it little by little.
When they emerge up to the hips, then tell her to push and make her sneeze with vinegar; for he will come out if God wishes it.
And if it does not emerge with that which I have narrated, then gradually bring the fetus back until you place him according to his natural shape. For he will come out then with an easy exit.
But if he is hindered with all that I have narrated, then take from mucilage of flaxseed, and sesame oil, and dissolved gum; and pound it all well in a mortar; then bind her vulva and the lower part of her womb with it. Then make her sit in warm water until she reaches the stage of labor pains.
When you see that his lower parts are already warm, then make her a fumigant of myrrh; and apply it to him. Then when he has taken the fumigation for one hour, make her sit on a stool. › Then make her sneeze: and bind her mouth and nose: and press the lower part of the belly with gentle compression. For the fetus will come out immediately.
The exit of the fetus is between the knees and hands. When it comes out in this manner, then she should insert her hands gradually. ︎ Then the woman should be laid back on her neck, and her feet should hang down; and she should lie on the bed, and she should wrap her hands. Then press gently above her belly. Then pull out what is under her feet from the cushions, until it is prepared at the lower part. But if the fetus does not come out, then take her feet and move them strongly. Then press gently above the hypochondrium until the fetus rises upwards. Then she should insert her hands and straighten the fetus gradually; and command the woman to push until the fetus comes out.
The exit of the fetus hanging laterally from the hands. She should insert her hand for its delivery. But if she cannot deliver it, then lift the woman and make her walk.
However, if she cannot walk, then lay her on the bed; and shake her legs vigorously. ︎ ︎
Then apply the poultice that you have prepared from the mucilages.
But if she is about to give birth, then make her sit on a stool. Then strive to deliver it by hand, and straighten the fetus according to its natural form; and make the woman sneeze, and command her to push until it comes out.
The exit of the fetus on its neck, with hands spread out, and its face is towards the back of its mother. The midwife should hold the fetus's hand, then slowly turn it and adjust it with ease.
When it has been adjusted, place on its lips what we have spoken of from oil and mucilages.
Then order her to move slowly. When you have done this, then make her sit on a chair and order her to lean to the right side. Then tell her to press down and make her sneeze with your help.
The exit of the prepared fetus is on the side. When it has descended to the opening of the womb along with the afterbirth in this manner, then cut the afterbirth with your nail until it is expelled from the moisture.  />
If it hangs over the face and neck of the fetus, then cut it from the navel so that it is not retained and causes death.
Then push the fetus inside until you place it as necessary, and tell the woman to press herself several times, for it will come out easily.
The exit of twins or many fetuses.  />  />  />  /> Know that twins often are born and sometimes three, and four are born. However, this is unusual and rarely happens.
Five is against nature and they do not live at all. Even if they multiply, one afterbirth contains them all, and they are separated by a membrane distinguishing between the ligament of each one's navel.
And sometimes they come out as one fetus comes out naturally and easily through the birth canal, and they come out in an admirable way, as we have said.  />  />  />  />  />
But if some of them are difficult during birth and reach the condition we have mentioned from unnatural shapes, then treat them as we have said: and let the midwife be skillful and do what she does with ease and delay, and she should adapt to every shape along with what is prepared for her by her guiding wisdom towards health.  />  />  />  />  />  />  />  />  />  />  />  />
Recollection of what is formed in the womb from embryos and then miscarried.
Sometimes one is formed in the womb, or two, three, four, five, six, seven, and sometimes more than ten: and indeed I have seen with my own eyes a woman miscarry seven, and another fifteen, all of them formed.
This was accomplished by the measurement of the glorious wise man.
Therefore, all this should be within the knowledge of the obstetrician. For perhaps something similar to that will happen to her: therefore she should oppose it with what is necessary.
Chapter 76
¶ On the extraction of a dead fetus.
When you are treating a dead fetus with the division I mentioned in the treatment, and it does not come out, and you are forced to use manual intervention, then you should consider this.
If therefore the woman is of sound constitution and not suffering from any of the conditions that might cause her to be lost, then it is necessary for the woman to be placed on her back on a bed, with her head tilted downwards and her legs raised; and let a midwife hold her by both sides or tie her to the bed so that her body does not move during the extraction of the fetus.
Then moisten the mouth of the womb with moist oils and linseed, and fenugreek seed mucilage.
Then the midwife should anoint her hand with these oils and mucilages; then she should introduce it into the womb with ease. Then let her seek with it the place where she can grab the hooks from the fetus and the places suitable for this.
Therefore consider then, if the fetus is ready to descend head first: then insert the hooks into its eyes, or its neck, or its mouth, or its palate, or under its chin, or in its shoulder blades, or in places near the ribs and under the hypochondria. ︎
If however the descent is upon his feet, then in the comb and middle ribs of him.
And he should hold the hook with his right hand and place its curvature between the fingers of his left hand. He should then easily insert it with his hand and fix the hook in one of those places that we have mentioned until it reaches the empty space.
Then he should insert another hook or a third one, if necessary, on the opposite side so that there is an equal contraction and it does not deviate to one side.
Then it should be stretched equally and not only straight but moved in every direction to facilitate its exit, just as is done with a tooth when it is extracted.
And between that, there should be something to soften the stretching. If a part is retained from it, then the midwife should anoint some fingers with oil and insert them to roll out whatever is retained.
If therefore a part of the fetus emerges, then they should change the hooks to a higher place: do this until the entire fetus comes out.
If therefore a hand emerges before the other and it is not possible to return it due to its constriction, then they should wrap a cloth around it. Then draw it out until when the whole emerges; cut it either at the junction of the sole or at the elbow: and thus you should do with the other hand and both feet.
If however the fetal head is large or it encounters constriction during birth or there is water collected on its head, then they should insert a thorny spatula between the fingers and shred the head with it to extract the water or break it with an instrument called Almisdac: the shape of which comes with the shapes of the other instruments in the chapter that follows this.
Similarly, do this if the fetus has a large head by nature: then it is necessary to cut away the alkengematu; or extract it with misdach, as we have said. Then draw out the bones with forceps.
If the head comes out but is constricted at the shoulders, then it should be cut until the fluid from the chest is released.
If however it does not become entangled nor yield to delivery, then cut off the head in pieces, as much as you are able.
If there is a tumor or swelling below the navel, or if it is caused by dropsy, then you should pierce it until the fluid runs out of it.
However, if the fetus is on its feet, then its extraction is easy and its direction towards the mouth of the womb is straightforward.
If however it is constricted at the abdomen or chest, then you should extract it with a cloth wrapped around your hand; and cut open the abdomen or chest until the fluid runs out of them.
If however the other members are extracted and only the head remains, then the midwife should insert her left hand. If therefore the mouth of the womb is open, then she should insert her hand deep into the womb and seek out the head with it, and draw it towards the mouth of the womb with her fingers; then she should insert a hook or two hooks into it, and draw it out with them.
If the mouth of the womb is constricted due to a hot tumor that has occurred there, then it should not be labored upon, but rather warm and oily substances should be administered; and apply poultices; and sit in waters that soften and moisten.
If the fetus is lying on its side, then it may turn; then administer what we have said for a living fetus.
If that is not possible, then it should be cut piece by piece and extracted.
And you must not leave anything from the placenta inside at all.
When therefore you have completed your operation, then administer what we said for hot swellings that occur in the womb.
If a flow of blood occurs, let it descend into stiptic waters, and administer the remaining cure.
And indeed I have already seen a woman in whose womb a dead fetus was; then she became pregnant with another in its place, after which another fetus also died. Therefore, after a long time, an abscess occurred in her navel, and it became swollen until it was opened: and it began to emit pus.
I was therefore called for her cure, and I treated her over a long time: but the wound did not heal.
I therefore placed upon it some strong drawing plasters: and a mouth came out from that place. Then some days passed for her, and another mouth came out. I was therefore amazed by this, since there is no mouth in the womb.
I therefore thought that they were from the bones of the dead fetus.
I therefore searched the wound and extracted many bones, while the woman was in a better condition; and she has now lived thus for a long time, and sends forth from that place only a little pus.  />
And I would not have introduced this foreign matter here, except that it contains knowledge and assistance for what the medical artist administers with his hand in a cure.
Chapter 77.
§ On the forms of the necessary instruments for fetal extraction.
The shape of the vertigo which opens the womb.
Here below is the form of the straps with which books are bound, having two windings at the ends of two pieces of wood, each being equal to the other. Verily, this vertigo should be made of more delicate silk, and to make it, either from ebony or boxwood.
And the width of each piece of wood is as if two fingers, and the edge of each is as one finger, and the length of each is a palm and a half; and in the middle of the two pieces of wood there are two additions of the same type of wood, which are already fixed on both sides, whose length is more or less half a palm, and the width of each is as if two fingers, or more or less.
And these two additions are inserted into the opening of the womb, so that it may be opened with them when you roll up the two vertigines.
Another shape, similar to it, more delicate and lighter.
It should be made of ebony or boxwood, according to the likeness of forceps. However, at the end of it there should be two additions, as you see here above; and the length of each addition is as if a palm, and the width of each is as two fingers.
Therefore, when you wish to open the womb with it, then make the woman sit on the bed with her feet hanging down, and that which is between her legs being open.  \\ Then insert these two joined additions into the womb; and you are holding the end of the instrument below between her thighs. Then open your hand with the instrument, as you do with forceps, equally according to the amount that you wish for the opening of the mouth of the womb, until the midwife does what she wants.
The shape of another vertigo which the ancients called the form of the expeller by which the fetus is expelled.
The shape of the Almisdal, by which a large head is crushed; and it resembles a forceps, which has teeth at the end, as you see.
And sometimes it is made like a pair of tongs, as you see here in this shape, which has teeth like the teeth of a saw, with which it is cut and crushed.
The shape of a vice with one spike.
The shape of a vice having two spikes.
The shape of scissors having two ends for cutting off the head.
The shape of two wide scissors as well.
All these instruments are used, and the more their forms are multiplied and prepared by the craftsman, the faster he is at his work and the higher he is esteemed among men for their number.
Therefore, do not despise any of these instruments, so that it may be prepared by you. For their necessity is inexcusable.
Chapter LXXVIII.
¶ On the Extraction of a Second Twin. xspace 🚫
When a second twin is retained at birth, then you should advise the woman to hold her breath. Then make her sneeze with you: and place your hand over her mouth and nose.  /> If it then emerges by this method, that is good.
If not, then take a pot and pierce a hole in its lid. Place in it the following opening-the-womb herbs: calamint, rue, dill, chamomile, anise, cassia bark, and centaury. Take all these herbs or some of them, submerge them in water, and place them over a fire.
Then place a reed in the hole of the pot's lid, with the other end in the mouth of the womb, and let her hold it until the steam reaches the cavity of the womb.
Then make her sneeze, as we said. For the afterbirth will come out easily.
But if it remains after this treatment and does not come out, then instruct the midwife to dip her hand in sesame oil or thickened mallow juice. Then she should insert it into the vagina and search for the afterbirth with it. When she has found it, then she should take hold of it and gently pull it out.
But if it is attached deep within the womb, then she should insert her hand as we have described until she finds the afterbirth and draws it out little by little straight forward so that the womb does not suddenly contract; rather it should gently shift from side to side. Then increase the pulling force gradually. In this way she will comply and be saved and escape from being stuck.
But if the mouth of the womb is narrowed as we have already described, care for her with sneezing and potions made from herbs.
But if it does not come out despite all these efforts, be careful not to tire yourself with repeated attempts at extraction.
Instead, whatever comes out towards the mouth of the womb should be tied to the woman's thigh.  Then give her an enema with four-ingredient ointment.  For it will decay after a few days and be expelled.
However, when it begins to decay, the smell will rise to her head and stomach and harm her. Therefore, appropriate fumigations should be administered for that purpose.
Some of the ancients have already found that a fumigation of nasturtium and dried figs is effective for this. 
The design of the device used to fumigate a woman who has retained her afterbirth or menses.  
Make something similar to alcama or from mustard seed: and place the broad end over the fire: and the smoke should be placed above the embers: hold it until that smoke is consumed: and repeat with another.
Chapter 79.
Of the treatment of unperforated anus.
Many infants are born whose anus is not perforated, which a soft syringe has already probed. Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that with her finger; and if not, let her pierce it with a sharp probe, and be careful that her arm does not touch him.
Then place a wool cloth soaked in wine and oil upon him. Then care for him with salves until he is cured.
However, if you fear that it will become blocked again, then place a lead tube in the opening for many days, and remove it when the child wants to defecate. ️
And now, obstruction of the anus also occurs due to the healing of a wound or an abscess. Therefore, it is necessary that that healing be cut out; then treat it as we have said with the treatment and lead.
Chapter 80.
¶ Of the treatment of fistulas that occur in the lower part.
The fistulas that occur in the lower part are nodules and swellings that occur near the anus externally; or within the space of one part; and there is one fistula, or many. ️ ️
Therefore, when that nodule becomes chronic, it opens, and from it flows an aqueous white fluid, or thin pus. ️ ️ ️
And sometimes these fistulas are penetrating. Therefore, penetrating ones are known by what comes out from defecation and flatulence when the patient uses defecation; and perhaps a worm comes out of them. ️
And among them are fistulas when they penetrate into the space of the bladder and to the urethral orifice. And among them are those that penetrate to the hip joint and to the tailbone.
The way to distinguish whether a fistula penetrates to the anus, even if it does not penetrate, is this: insert your index finger into the anus and insert a fine probe made of iron or brass into the fistula when there is no curvature.
But if there is curvature, then insert into it a fine probe made of lead or a horsehair until you feel the probe or hair with your finger.
If you do not feel it at all, and nothing comes out of the opening upon emptying, nor is there any gas or worm as I have said, then know that it is not penetrating; hasten to its cure.
And when the fistula penetrates to the bladder or the urethral opening, then its indication is the passage of urine from it; and its cure is to close off this passage so that the area may be healed with medicine.
But if it penetrates to the hip joint or the mouth of the hip, then its sign is that a probe reaches there if there is no curvature up to the mouth; and finding pain around the part, and that pus always comes out from it; and that medication does not help it, nor does it heal with ointment.
And in all these penetrating fistulas there is no cure at all; and their cure is labor and vanity for the foolish doctor who attempts it.
But in that which is not penetrating and is not old, healing with a saw is hoped for; as I have told you, and I have already proved it: and the procedure is this, that the patient lies on his back between your hands; and raise his legs up to above his hips, and let his hips be bent toward his abdomen. Then he should insert a probe of lead or iron into the fistula, if there is tortuosity, until he knows where the probe has arrived.
But if the patient feels it around the anus, then you should insert your index finger into the anus.
Therefore, if you feel the probe has already penetrated through the body and beyond what you feel between your finger and the fistula or skin, then know for certain that it is a penetrating fistula; do not labor on it, for there is no cure for it, as we have said.
However, it is said that in some people the flesh heals and from the medication by which it is hoped for help, let a fine cautery be ignited according to the width of the fistula as previously mentioned, and insert the burning cautery into the fistula until it reaches the anus. Then repeat this two or three times until you know that all those added fleshy parts, which are like a bird's feather quill, have been burned away.
Then treat it with linen cloths wrapped in butter until the burned flesh comes out; then treat it with ointments that generate flesh and strengthen it.
If it heals, that is good.
And if not, then it will never be cured by any other treatment.
And if the probe comes out and does not reach your finger which is in the anus, and there is a thick membrane of flesh or skin between it and the probe, and you see that the fistula follows the surface of the skin, then cut the skin from the beginning of the fistula and proceed cutting along with the probe that is in the fistula until the cutting reaches where the tip of the probe was, and the probe is released and falls out.
Then clean those fleshy parts that are like a bird's feather quill, so that nothing remains of them.
If blood overcomes you and loosens between you and your surgery so that it separates those flesh pieces, then it is better for a quicker healing to cauterize them with fire or with sharp medicine.
Because a cautery with fire brings together good conditions: the burning of those flesh pieces, and the cutting off of blood, and the drying out of moisture.
Then care for it with bandages wrapped in butter or crushed cabbage leaves until the place releases pus, and those burnt flesh pieces come out in the pus.
Then care for the wound with healing ointments that produce hard flesh; and there are medicines which contain astringents and drying agents.
For when they are restored, then it is healed: and you should not fear recurrence.
But if the fistula has already reached as far as the deep part of the anus and is lengthened by the body's excess, then insert your finger into the anus and search with it.  />
Therefore if you feel a swelling and there is a membrane of silk or flesh between you and it, which is close to penetrating, then the operation on that [fistula] is not possible except by way of hope and expectation.
That is, because in it [the fistula] one of three methods is applied: either to cauterize it as we said, or to cut it away until you reach its concavity so that it is possible for you to insert bandages and immediate care. And do not proceed much with the cutting so that you do not cut into the band that contains the anus and cause an unfortunate exit of excrement without will. Then care for it with what we said.  />  />
Perhaps it will heal; or else you lengthen the membrane itself and cleanse it after you have cut it almost to the anus, as we said, either with a probe or with some other sharp instrument.  />  />  />  />  />  /> Then cleanse those filtered meats that are in the incision as far as you can with probing.
Then attempt the restoration of the entire wound with the incision and the upper opening where it heals; and there will remain an open fistula in the interior part of the anus, and it will be easier for the patient.
And sometimes the fistula occurs in this manner: and it is when you insert a probe into the fistula and it is on the side of the anus near the surface of the body with skin and the edge of the anus; then take a perforated probe at the tip, which is like an aleskef needle, that is, prepared from rawhide, in this manner. And insert into it a thread wound with five threads, and about such. Then insert the probe with the thread into the fistula until it reaches its hollow part.
If therefore it penetrates near the inner edge of the anus, then draw out the thread from that opening; so that you insert your finger into the anus and extract the end of the thread, and bring together both ends at once; and tie each one, and leave it for one day or two days; and however more the thread cuts into the flesh, tie it well until those flesh parts between the two ends of the thread are cut off and fall away; then care for the wound until it heals.
If however the opening of the fistula is not penetrating: then cause it to penetrate by whatever manner you prepare for yourself, except if it is very deep. For indeed it is not for you to do that because of the arm [strength], so that you do not cut it.
Then deal with it as we said until it heals.
The form of a sharp spatule that is used to divide the fistula, whose curve is very sharp and the other part is not sharp, so that it does not cut what is unnecessary, as you see.
Chapter 81.
On the stitching of hemorrhoids from which blood flows due to their incision: and the care of fissures.
There are two types of hemorrhoids. For they are either within the anus, similar to small blisters or plums, or as if they were grains of grapes themselves. And from them are small and large ones: and blood always flows from them, whether there is one or many. And they are outside the anus, and at its edges.
However, those that are outside the anus are for the most part moist and of little water, from which flows yellowish water or a small amount of blood with constant discharge: and they are the color of the body.
And its treatment, when it is within the anus, is that you order the patient to sit down: and let it be squeezed out until the anus protrudes and appears to you like a hemorrhoid. Therefore, hang them with hooks or hold them with your fingernail.  Then cut them at their roots.
If hooks do not hold them because of their moisture and softness, then take them with a rough cloth or a piece of woolen material and pull them out with your fingers. Then cut them, and after the cutting, sprinkle some hot powders on them so that they act as a caustic. Or cauterize them according to what has been said in the chapter on cauterization.   Then treat them with the remaining treatment until they heal.
If the anus does not protrude, then give the patient an enema containing a mild purgative, so that it washes with what is in the anus and quickly obeys the expulsion when the patient presses.
If the worms are outside from the anus, then their nature is light and easy. And it is as if you take them with your fingernail or take them with a hook, and cut them off. Then care for them with what we have said until they heal.
And if someone is repelled by the incision with iron, then it is necessary for you to apply their stitches in this manner. Take a thread wound around itself and insert it into a needle. Then draw out the worm upwards and make it penetrate with the needle into its root on the other side; and wrap the two ends of the thread around the lower part of the needle in a broad manner, and tighten the worm with a strong constriction. Then tie the thread and withdraw the needle.
Do this with all the worms, and leave one out of them; do not remove it so that the blood can flow out from there.
Then place on the anus a cloth soaked in rose oil or cedar oil and put it on the anus; and instruct the patient to rest. Then leave him until it falls off.
So when the worms fall out, care for them with ointments and other treatments until they heal.
¶ On the Care of Fissures For it often happens from the drying out of feces and the constriction of nature.
Therefore, when they become chronic and medicine is ineffective on them, then it is necessary that you shave them with the point of a spatula or with your fingernail until they become moist, and remove from them the upper skin which prevents them from healing. Then care for them until they heal as is necessary.
But if they do not heal, then shave them with a more severe scraping than the first until they bleed profusely; and then care for them until they heal.
"About treating inverted and uninverted almirma, as well as athelil scars and formicae.
"Chapter Eighty-Two.
"Know that almirmar is nothing but a round knot of the color of the body, similar to the head of a nail; and it occurs throughout the body, especially in the lower parts of the feet and toes; and from this comes pain during walking.
"Therefore, it should be cut around like the head of a nail and held with tweezers or a hook, and removed from its root.
"Then treat it; and if you wish, cauterize it as explained in its chapter.
"Athelil, however, is one small rough and pitted roundness above the surface of the body. "And they often occur on children's hands.
"Its treatment is that you stretch the athelil and cut it, or bind it with a silk thread or a hair until it falls off. "And if you wish, cauterize it with fire or with a sharp medicine, as mentioned before, and now inverted and uninverted athelil will be removed with the instrument that I will describe.
"Formica, however, is also a small rough and pitted raised area on the surface of the body, going very deep; and when cold touches it, it feels like an ant bite, and this occurs throughout the body, but most often on the hands.
"Its treatment is to take a small tube made from a goose feather or a strong vulture feather; and place this tube over the formica until the circumference of the tube contains its edges. "Then roll your hand with the tube until it cuts through the edges of the formica; and place it deeply into the flesh, removing the formica from its root.
And if you wish, make that with an air tube or iron tube, according to this shape.
Let the upper part of the tube be at the height, pulling the swab wrapped around it so that its grasp and rolling off are lessened.
And if you wish, burn the formica as mentioned in the section on burning athelil in the chapter on the cautery.
Chapter 83.
About the shapes of instruments used for enemas in diseases of the anus and for relieving flatulence and colic.
Sometimes an enema is made of silver, or copper, or cast bronze, or hammered iron.  /> ¶ Et si uis, fac eum ex quercu, secundum hanc formam:
And sometimes it is made from these instruments, both small and large, according to those in which they are administered.
Therefore, what is administered for the treatment of small children should be small; and whatever their anus is weak or painful, thus also should be the enema.  /> ¶ Illud autem quod administratur in curatione adultorum sit magnum.
Large enema.
The tube of it, that is the upper end where the bladder is tied, should be wide like this: and there should be a distinct part so that the bladder can be tied as you see, and its lower end which enters the anus should be blunt, that is not open, very smooth, pulling to subtlety; and on one side of it there should be two holes, and on the other side one hole.
And the width of the hole should be according to the thickness of the rays, and slightly thicker; and let the bladder in which the medicines are placed be from a pig's bladder or from sheepskin that is according to the shape of a small asparagus leaf, whose stem is one palm long.  /> ¶ Et sit canna eius uel argentea, uel ex aere fuso.
And let it be pierced with many holes as if rolled out, and let there be a space between each hole the thickness of a finger. Then put into those holes a thread of raw silk, which should be made up of ten threads or about that number, and attach to it a bag like an esophagus. When the bag is put into it, let the enema be tied at the head between two restricting ligatures with a strong constriction. Then give an enema with it.
And this is the shape of the bag here depicted, and of the holes.
The quality of giving an enema with it is this: that you fill the bag or bladder with medicine that has been heated according to the patient's tolerance; and be careful that it is not too hot nor too cold.
Then let the patient lie on their back and lift up their legs; and place under them an intahaan, that is, a hide on which people lie, or a cloth.
Then anoint the end of the enema with oil, or with the white of an egg, or with a thickening made from fenugreek, or similar substances. Then introduce it into the anus gently. Then let the attendant take the bag with both hands at once and squeeze it forcefully until all the contents of the enema have been expelled into the intestine.  ?>
Then remove the enema, and let the patient raise their legs against the wall.
If the medicine causes him to move his bowels, then he should hold it as long as possible. And if he sleeps with it the whole night through, it is more beneficial.
But if you give him an enema during an attack of diarrhea and his discharge is rapid; then repeat the enema until he is well.
But if there are hemorrhoids or painful boils in the anus, then let the enema be very fine and gentle, like those used to give enemas to children.
And let this be the form of a fine enema on which the skin is tight.
Chapter 84
I have already spoken in the division on the treatment of wounds what was fitting for a book, and here I will speak about their treatment both with hands and with medicines according to their due course.
Therefore, I say that wounds are diversified according to what causes the wound, and according to the place upon which the wound falls.
The things by which wounds are made are often like the throwing of a stone: or the cut of a sword, or a knife: or striking with a spear, or a stick, or an arrow: and similar things from many objects.
But the wounds that are made according to places of the body are such as a wound which falls upon the head, or the neck, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver: and similar from those members.
And I am relating the treatment of some wounds so that I may put forth that reasoning and rule upon other wounds.
And I will begin with simple head wounds, since the reminder of compounded (wounds) will come at the beginning of chapter three.
Therefore, I say: If a simple wound occurs in the head and there is no broken bone, then consider whether it is from the throwing of a stone or similar objects and has already torn only the skin: and it is a large wound and you fear an unfavorable outcome from hot inflammation: then hasten and perform a phlebotomy immediately, do not delay it; and draw out some blood according to its strength, if there is nothing preventing the phlebotomy, especially if the amount of blood coming out of the wound is small. And let the phlebotomy be from the opposite side of the wounded part.
And let the phlebotomy be from the opposite side of the wounded part. And let the patient beware of overeating, wine, and heavy foods.
But if anything prevents him from eating in moderation, then let him be fed less, and let him not approach meats or wine.
And place on the wound, if a hot abscess forms, only boiled linseed oil, or with wine that has been boiled down to a thick syrup.
But if you are confident that a hot abscess will not form, then place on the wound, if it is fresh with its own blood and has not been exposed to the air, the powder that I will describe shortly: and if the wound has already been exposed to the air, then apply certain ointments until it heals.
But if the wound is large, or is from a sword cut and similar things, and its lips do not come together by themselves, then bring them together with stitching, as I will describe in the chapter on wounds of the abdomen regarding their stitching.
But if the wound has already been laid open to the bone and hangs loose, and there is no obstacle to its healing except for a small flap of skin, then cut away that flap. Then treat the wound with medicines and restore to it hard flesh in place of skin. And instruct the patient to be fed foods that are thick, such as grain porridge, until it becomes like a porridge, and similar foods.
But if you find rotting flesh that does not adhere to the bone, then cut away all of the rotten flesh and cast it aside; then treat the wound.
But if in these wounds there is an artery or vein from which blood flows and it does not close by itself with medicines, then search for the artery. Therefore, if you find that it is not cut through, then cut it with a sharp instrument or tie it off. If necessity requires it when that which I have said is of no use, then cauterize it until the blood is cut off.
If, however, these wounds are small and simple, then their condition is easy and light: so that you should sprinkle this powder over them, for it consolidates them before the air changes them.
The Method of the Flesh-making Powder. Take one part frankincense, two parts dragon's blood, and three parts of unslaked lime. Grind all together thoroughly, and sift it. Fill the wound with this powder, and bind it well until it adheres firmly to it and coagulates with the blood.
Then bind it above with fine cloths, and leave it untouched, not unbinding it until it is well healed so that it does not open again. For the medicine is not removed from it until it is healed.
And sometimes lime alone does this, when you do not have frankincense at hand; and dragon's blood also performs the same operation in many of the great wounds, when it is placed upon them and bound, and they are recent wounds with their own blood, which the air has not altered.
But if the air has already altered them in some way, especially when it is summertime, then this powder is not intended for such a position; therefore, care for it with what I have said, placing upon it certain digestive unguents, or place upon it poultices made from barley flour mixed with water and honey until they emit pus. 》 Then care for them with the remaining treatment until they are healed.
But if a fracture occurs with the wound and it is small, then extract that with forceps; and I will now speak of the treatment of skull fractures in what follows.
About Wounds of the Neck
If however a wound occurs on the neck, then there is no difference between it and a simple head wound in terms of treatment.
But if a nerve of the neck or an artery has already been cut: then if it is a nerve, there is no remedy for it except to avoid treating it with anything that causes strong coagulation, such as ziniar, and zegi, and similar things. Because they harm nerves and contract them.
And do not put anything cold at all on the wound: because the substance of nerves is cold and its continuation is with the brain, which is higher than other members: and that which is used for treatment should be from mild medicines, such as lime washed with sweet water infused many times with oil or rose oil, and tuthia when it is also washed with sweet water: and other mineral stones according to this method, and moist ointments.
If however the wound is large, then apply a suture: or sew its lips together with silk threads. Then care for it until it heals.
But if the wound is deep or an abscess has formed at its lower part where pus is already accumulating, then pierce it in the deeper place of that part.
And if an artery has been cut in the wound and its blood flow has followed: then separate it or cut it off and tie it: or cauterize it if necessity demands that.
But if the thyroid cartilage has been cut, whether partially or completely and the alhaudegia are saved: then gather the lips of the skin with a suture over the tracheal cartilage, and do not touch the trachea, but rather make it even, and bring it back to its natural shape. ¨ Then tie it with a suitable bandage and leave it for several days. Then care for it with ointments that have astringency and drying properties until it heals.
But if the wound has already affected the bone, then explore it. And if there are fragments of bone in it, remove all of them or as many as you can. And whatever is not prepared, leave it until the wound becomes putrid and its outlet separates and loosens.
But if the wound is fresh, then sprinkle on it the powder I mentioned. However, if bone is visible in the wound and a fistula forms, then treat it with that which is mentioned in its chapter.
¶ About the Wound in the Ribs.
If it is a wound from a spear or knife and you see its depth, then consider [the following]: If air escapes from the wound when the patient exhales, know that the wound is fatal.
But if the wound is not deep and is fresh with its own blood, do not put powder on it from the first hour, nor bind it, so that the blood does not collect in its depth and return to the heart and kill the patient; but put an attractive ointment on it and loosen it twice a day. )))
If you do not have ointment at hand, then place an old cloth on the wound's opening so that it absorbs what comes out of it from moisture. And make sure the patient sleeps on the wound so that what accumulates in it is drained away.
But if three days or more have passed since the wound was inflicted and no spasm occurs to the patient, nor is there a bad tremor of the heart, nor constriction in breathing, and you see that its other symptoms are good: then know that the wound is safe. Care for it with compresses and the rest of the treatment until it heals.
But if its healing is delayed and it continually opens, then know that a fistula has already formed. Care for it according to the method described in its chapter.
And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut and is simple on the surface of the chest or back, then care for it with that which was previously described under stitching, if it is large; or with powder, if it is small.
But if the cut has already affected the bone and pieces have fallen out from it, then explore the wound and hasten to remove those pieces if they are separated. But if they are not separated, then leave them alone until the wound becomes foul, for their extraction will be facilitated.
For the treatment of other wounds occurring on other parts of the body, the judgment is the same as that which we have said.
¶ On Wounds of the Abdomen and Exit of Intestines and Their Treatment.
The disruption that occurs in the abdomen is great, medium, and small.
Therefore, in the case of a great disruption, sometimes an intestine or a number of intestines emerge. ‌
For this reason their insertion and suturing are more vigorous and difficult.
And a small disruption is also made difficult in another way. Therefore, their reduction will be more difficult if you do not hasten to return them immediately to their place; for it becomes distended, opens up, and swells, making its entrance difficult.
Therefore, a medium-sized disruption is better than other disruptions, because with it the reduction of the intestine is not difficult, as it is in these two kinds.
You should know that the suture of a vein is according to four methods.
Two common sutures are suitable for the suture of the abdomen and for the suture of other wounds of the body; two other sutures properly belong to other wounds. Nevertheless, they are more proper for the suture of the abdomen; and I will tell you each one with an explanation and demonstration.
I say therefore, that when the wound is small and something comes out of it from the intestine, and it becomes difficult to reduce it; then this is one of two methods. Or because of the smallness of the rupture, as we said; or because there is swelling in the intestine due to cold air.
Therefore, when this is the case, then you should heat it so that you submerge a sponge or a damp cloth in warm water alone. Or boil it in water with hyssop, pepper, and clove, and press the intestine with it until the swelling is resolved.
Sometimes it [the wound] produces wine that has astringent properties, and this is better than plain water for resolving the swelling.
Therefore, when you see that the swelling has been resolved, then moisten the intestine with water in which mallow or hollyhock has been boiled. For by this its passage is made easy with a small thing.
If, however, its return is delayed after this treatment, then find the small opening with the instrument by which hemorrhoids are cut.
And the first treatment is better when it is prepared than when it is cut; and there is no need to cut after necessity and the lack of an instrument. xspace
Let one part of it be twisted and sharp, and the other part not sharp; and its tip should not be very fine like a Spathamus, but rather somewhat blunt. And this resembles a hook, as you see.
When the wound is enlarged and the intestine protrudes, then it must be reduced to its natural shape in its proper place, if possible over it, because it is better.
When the disruption is large in the lower part of the belly, then you should make the patient lie on their back, and raise their legs higher than their head. And if it is in the upper part of the belly, then put his head and chest higher than his lower parts.
And likewise if the disruption is in one of the two parts of the belly, then direct your attention and consideration always to this: that the part where the wound is should be higher than the other part.
And thus you should do this for large wounds and medium-sized wounds.
But in small wounds, place it according to what is prepared for you.
Then make sure there is a pious assistant present between your hands, who holds the entire disruption with his hand: and join its lips together. Then let him who follows the stitching remove something from it, piece by piece: and this is the manner of a common single stitch. ‍
And it is that you should take one needle or several needles according to the size of the wound. Then leave from the end of the disruption a quantity equal to the ring finger, that is, of the physician; and insert one needle besides what you put into it thread in two ends of the skin, with two ends of the thread that is under the skin from inside until you make it penetrate from the other side, and now you have joined together two ends of the skin, and two ends of the thread: and there are four rows.
Then tighten with double thread around the needle several times from both sides together, until the two lips of the wound are joined in a decent union.
Then let go of the thickness of the finger and also insert another needle into it; afterwards pull it out with thread as you did with the first needle. And therefore do not cease doing this with what you need from needles until you complete the constriction of the entire wound.
And let the needles be of medium thickness between coarseness and fineness, because fine needles very quickly penetrate the flesh and thick ones have a difficult entry into the skin; therefore it is necessary that they be of medium fineness and coarseness.
And it is not necessary that the needle be inserted into the two ends of the nearby skin very closely, so that the flesh may not be quickly penetrated and the wound opened before its own healing, and also lengthened with the suture, preventing the wound from healing.
Then cut the ends of the needles so that they do not harm the patient in his sleep; and place little pads of cloth around all parts of them to hold the ends of the needles; and leave them there until you know that the wound is already healed.
And this particular type of suture with needles is more suitable for small wounds. Because one needle or two, or about that number, is sufficient for their suture.
However, the second type of suture is common, that you join with the suture the four ends: two ends of skin and two ends of sinew as one, with a needle on which there is an equally fine and coarse thread wound.
Then when you have penetrated these four ends with the needle, bring the needle back from the side where you began, so that the pulled thread falls from the upper part of the wound; let the suture be as the seam of a cloth by which clothes are sewn together, and place between every suture a quantity of the thickness of a smaller finger.
This stitching is known to people.
And with this stitching I healed a wound that had happened to a man in his abdomen, who had been wounded with a knife, and the tear of the wound was greater than one palm: and about two palms came out from the middle of the intestines, and there was a tear in the middle of the belly.
Therefore, I returned it after his intestine had been outside the wound for twenty-four hours.
Therefore, the wound healed in the space of about fifteen days; and I treated him, and he was cured; and he lived many years after that, converted to his former habits.
And the doctors had judged that it would not heal.
And from a miracle, it was that I did not treat it with ointment. Because I was in a place where no ointment could be found, nor anything from the medicines. Therefore, I placed an old cloth over the wound twice a day, and I continued to wash it with honey water until it was healed.
But there are two kinds of stitching that I will describe according to the narrative of the language.
And it is that you should begin with a sharp stitch; and introduce the needle from the outside part towards the inner part.
Therefore, when the needle penetrates into the skin and into the tendon that goes along the length and width of the entire body; leave the end of the thread on the side where you introduced the needle, and make it penetrate from the inner part to the outer part at the other end of the suture. ➤
When you have made it penetrate in this way at that end of the suture from the outer part to the inner part; then make it penetrate likewise at the same end from the outer part to the inner part; and leave the end of the thread, which is on this side, and make the needle penetrate into the other end from the inner part to the outer part; and continue to penetrate with your penetration as you make it penetrate into the end of the suture that is in that part, until it penetrates entirely. ➤
Then begin also from this same side, and either the very thing itself along with its tip, which is from the knife in the other side, and extract the needle from the skin that it penetrated.
Then bring it back into that skin, and either the tip of the needle, which is in the other side, with this tip of thread: and extract it from the skin on its part, and do this once and another; and do this once after the other, until its entirety is brought out externally according to that example.
And the end of this stitch is that just as there are stitches for peeling skins which are on skins, so also needles once from one side of the skin tip: and that you leave them once from another side, until you complete it.
The second kind of stitch which Galen called proper.
This statement has been narrated in such a way that some physicians do this according to the likeness, so that they bring together every part to its suitable companion by nature: and they apply the tip of the needle to its other tip, and the tip of thread to its other tip. And this is done as I tell you.
It is necessary that you drive the needle into the near end of the thread from you on the outer part, and make it penetrate to the inner in that only: and leave two tips of needle. Then turn the needle and make it penetrate from the outer part to the inner in the two tips of needle, that is on both sides.
Then turn both of them and also make both penetrate from the inner to the outer, into the two other ends of thread which are on the opposite side.  \\
And this method of stitching is better than common easy stitching, and it is the stitch whose mention preceded.
"This is therefore also the saying of Galen.
And some said. The stitching of the abdomen should be corrected with two needles. That is, you introduce one thread into both of them: and begin with the introduction of the needle from what is on your side, and make it penetrate to the other side, following the stitching of those who evenly sew hides.
And know that when there is a rupture in the middle of the abdomen, then its stitching is more difficult than in other places of the abdomen.
However, the judgment of treating a wound is the same as for other wounds.
That is, when you obtain a fresh wound with its own blood before the air alters it, and bring out the intestine, and sew it up, and make it firm, then place powdered kermes on it.
But if the air has already altered the wound, then place on it certain ointments which you have at hand, until they cause pus: and the threads fall out, and the silk and myrrh are strengthened. Then care for it as is the care of other wounds, until it heals.
But if the medications are not at hand, then place on it immediately from when it begins to emit pus, old cotton: and change it twice a day, as I have taught you, until it heals.
For you do not need another treatment in many cases, when the wounds are simple.  />
But if you fear that the wound may communicate with the main members during injury, then it is necessary to soak a soft wool cloth in warm oil or rose oil, and place it around the areas between the groins and under the armpits.
But if he feels pain or pricking or putrefaction in his intestines (for this often happens), then enema him with warm stiptic wine, especially if the putrefaction has already reached the intestine and caused a piercing exitus up to its concavity.
And know that what is from the large intestine is of easier healing, and what is from them is from the small intestine, more difficult to heal.
And the intestine which is called jejunum does not accept healing from a wound that occurs in it at all; and this is due to its multitude of veins and their size, and due to the fineness of its body, and the proximity of the nature of the nerves themselves.
But if what comes from the wound is a cord and you find it fresh, reintroduce it according to your usual method of reducing intestines equally.
But if a length of time has passed and it has already turned green or black, then you must tie it with thread over the darkened part to prevent bleeding from happening. For in a cord there are veins and arteries.
Then cut what is beyond that ligature and place the two ends of the thread hanging from the lower part of the wound outside it: so that its traction upon you is alleviated, and the pulling out of it in the case of a cord, and the discharge of pus from the wound.
§ Remembering the Wound that Occurs in the Intestine.
When an injury occurs in the intestine and it is small, then it is possible for it to be restored in some men, because I saw a man who was wounded in his belly with a lance thrust, and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and the wound healed, and a fistula formed, and from it came discharge and gas. )))
I therefore applied treatment until I did not trust in his healing; nor did I cease to examine it closely, until the place was healed and consolidated.
After I saw that the place had already healed, I feared for the patient that a similar misfortune would occur in his abdomen; and this misfortune did not happen to him from that time onward. And he remained in his better condition, eating and drinking, having intercourse, entering the bath, and exercising according to his diet.
And some of those who perform experiments have said that when there is a wound in the intestine and it is small, then it should be ligated in this manner. And it is necessary to take ants with large heads. Then bring together the two lips of the wound and place one of those ants whose mouths are open on the two lips of the wound. Therefore, when it bites onto them and tightens its mouth, cut off its head, for it will stick, and not come loose.
Then place another ant near the first one, and do not stop doing this with ants, one after the other, according to the entire extent of the wound.
Then return him, and his wound. For those heads remain attached in the intestine until the intestine is healed and there is no further harm to the patient at all.
And it is also possible to ligate the intestine even with a fine thread: that which has been taken out of the intestine of an animal, attached to it after it is inserted into a needle.
And it is necessary to take the end of this thread from the intestine, and scrape off much of its flesh. Then tie a fine linen thread at its end. Then insert that thread into a needle and sew the intestine with it. Then return him to his rupture.
And this method of suturing with ants and intestine is only according to the way of faith and hope. />
You should know that a large and deep wound, especially if it is in one of the thin intestines, then there is no remedy except to cauterize, and it will not heal at all.
On the Care of Zukhemen and Fistulas
You should know that any wound or abscess when it becomes old and chronic and turns into an ulcer and does not heal and always discharges pus and does not come to a head: then it is called generally in whatever member it may be a Fistula, and we call this Zuchemen.
And indeed a Fistula is in truth a knotty, hard, white, filtered ulcer, with which there is no pain, having the concavity of a bird's feather; and because of this some call it Risati, that is, a feather.
And at certain times it is moist, discharging pus. And sometimes the moisture may break up at certain hours. And this moisture may be sometimes much and sometimes little; thick sometimes and other times thin.
And I have already mentioned this in the division, when I said "wounds," that any ulcer which does not heal and in which no flesh is generated, it is only for one of nine causes.
One of these causes is either because of the scarcity or poor quality of blood in the body; or because there is hard flesh between it and its lips, preventing the birth of new flesh; or because it contains much filth and impurity; or because the ulcer itself is putrid and the material sent to it is of bad quality; or because the medicine used for its treatment is not suitable; or because a falling corruption in the region is pestilential, or because of some property specific to that region, as happens in Caesaraugusta, where the digestion of diseases is difficult and the natural healing of abscesses is delayed; or because there is one bone, or a number of bones, within it. ︎
And I have already shown all these causes and their signs, and the treatments of them with medicines by division; and here it is necessary for me to make you know the treatment of Fistula and Cyst, which is done by the way of operation with the hand.
Therefore, know that a Fistula can occur in all the members of the body.
